801 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Pickens v. State


No. F-90-1297


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 74; 885 P.2d 678; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 84; 65 O.B.A.J. 3842



November 14, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Pickens v. State, 2001 OK CR 3, 19 P.3d 866, 2001 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2 (Okla. Crim. App., 2001)
Related proceeding at Pickens v. Cook, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 51467 (N.D. Okla., Apr. 18, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CREEK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DONALD D. THOMPSON, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED for NEW TRIAL


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Creek County (Oklahoma), entered a judgment convicting defendant of first degree murder, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7, feloniously carrying a firearm, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1283, and robbery with firearms after former conviction of two or more felonies, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 801. He was sentenced to death, 10 years, and life imprisonment, respectively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed a convenience store and shot and killed he clerk. When he was interviewed and arraigned, defendant confessed. He was convicted of first degree murder, feloniously carrying a firearm, and robbery with firearms after former conviction of two or more felonies. Defendant was sentenced to death, ten years, and life imprisonment, respectively. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial. In reaching its decision, the court held that defendant's videotaped confession was inadmissible because he had not waived his Fifth and Sixth Amendment rights to counsel. The court further held that the admission of the confession was not harmless error. Also, the court held that the trial court's failure to instruct on the lesser included noncapital offenses was not harmless because, even if the jury found that defendant's PCP intoxication prevented him from forming the specific intent necessary for murder, it had no option but to acquit or convict defendant of first degree murder. Finally, the court held that the information did not adequately allege each element of first degree murder under malice, felony murder, or both, as required by law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment convicting defendant of first degree murder, feloniously carrying a firearm, and robbery with firearms after former conviction of two or more felonies. The case was remanded for a new trial.

 

802 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. State


No. F-92-678


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 70; 884 P.2d 1186; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 78; 65 O.B.A.J. 3356



October 18, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 6, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 91. Released for Publication December 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DANIEL L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which after a jury trial, convicted him of first degree malice aforethought murder, robbery with a dangerous weapon, larceny of an automobile, first degree rape, and forcible anal sodomy. He also challenged the sentence of death imposed after the second phase of the bifurcated trial.


OVERVIEW: In challenging his conviction and sentence, defendant raised 34 claims of error, many of which the court found were either waived by his failure to object during trial or which did not satisfy the plain error standard for reversal. With respect to errors which had not been waived, the court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's admission of an autopsy photograph of the victim because the photograph was relevant and its probative value was not outweighed by its potential for prejudice. The court found that the Oklahoma rape shield statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2412 (1992), was applicable though the victim was dead. Given that and the fact that consent was not an issue in the case, the court found that the trial court did not err in prohibiting defendant from cross-examining a witness who dated the victim about his sexual relations with her. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict and that because defendant claimed he was innocent of the murder, he was not entitled to a jury instruction on lesser-included offenses. The court found no error in either the jury instructions or the presentation of evidence during the sentencing phase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence.

 

803 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Neill v. State


No. F-92-975


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 69; 896 P.2d 537; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 79; 65 O.B.A.J. 3369



October 13, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 27, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMANCHE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JACK BROCK, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of murder in the first degree in violation of Okla. Code Crim. P., Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981); shooting with intent to kill in violation of Okla. Code Crim. P., Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 652 (1981); and attempted shooting with intent to kill in violation of Okla. Code Crim. P., Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 652 (1981). He was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered three bank employees during a bank robbery. He also killed a bank customer and severely wounded other customers. During the incident, defendant also shot at an infant, who was not killed because defendant was out of bullets. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and sentences. The court first found that the State of Oklahoma's impression that one juror would be sympathetic to defendant's religious beliefs was a legitimate, race-neutral reason to strike the juror. There were no other jury selection errors. The court next found that evidence of what defendant did within the three days after the robbery and murders was admissible because it was so closely-related to the robbery and murders as to form a logical connection. As to the sentencing, the court determined that the admission of testimony from the victims' relatives did not deny defendant his right to a fair sentencing proceeding under Okla. Code Crim. P., Okla. Stat. tit. 22, §§ 984, 984.1, 991a(C). Finally, a finding that the murders were especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel was supported by the evidence because of the extreme mental anguish suffered by the bank employees prior to their deaths.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

804 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. State


Case No. F-89-508


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 66; 887 P.2d 301; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 76; 65 O.B.A.J. 3261



September 30, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 18, 1995. Released for Publication January 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CLIFFORD E. HOPPER, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with first degree malice aforethought murder, assault and battery with a dangerous weapon, and assault with a dangerous weapon. The jury found him guilty, and the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) sentenced him to death for the murders and imposed prison terms for the other offenses. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took a knife and went to the trailer where his girlfriend lived with their baby, intending to take the baby and leave. When he was told that the baby could not go with him, defendant became angry and stabbed to death both his girlfriend and her uncle. Defendant claimed that the trial judge erred in admitting photographs of his girlfriend's body and a tape recording of her emergency telephone call made during the attack and in refusing to give an instruction on first degree manslaughter. The court upheld defendant's conviction and the sentence imposed. The court ruled that (1) the probative value of the photographs outweighed the danger of unfair prejudice because the number of the wounds depicted tended to support the state's theory that the murders were premeditated; (2) the recording from the telephone call had no probative value, but its admission was harmless because there was overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt; and (3) the refusal to give a first degree manslaughter instruction was proper because the evidence did not support such an instruction and defendant's theory of defense was that he committed second-degree murder rather than first-degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentences for first degree malice aforethought murder, assault and battery with a dangerous weapon, and assault with a dangerous weapon.

 

805 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Medlock v. State


No. C-91-298


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 65; 887 P.2d 1333; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 74; 65 O.B.A.J. 3237



September 30, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 9, 1995. Released for Publication February 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CANADIAN COUNTY. THE HONORABLE EDWARD C. CUNNINGHAM, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: The Judgment and Sentence is AFFIRMED. The Application for Writ of Certiorari is DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to first degree murder with malice aforethought, and the District Court of Canadian County (Oklahoma) imposed the death penalty. Defendant filed an application for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered a young girl by putting her head in a toilet and stabbing her neck with a knife. He gave a full confession to the police. He initially pleaded not guilty by reason of insanity, but later entered a plea of guilty. At the sentencing hearing, defendant presented evidence that he suffered from multiple personality disorder. Before his sentence was pronounced, defendant filed an application to withdraw his guilty plea. Defendant claimed that the lower court erred in denying his application to withdraw his plea and in imposing the death penalty. The court held that (1) defendant's failure to raise the issue of the factual sufficiency of the plea in his application to withdraw the plea constituted a waiver and the lower court did not commit plain error by failing to order sua sponte the withdrawal of his plea; (2) the evidence supported the lower court's conclusion that defendant was not insane; (3) defendant failed to show that his attorney rendered ineffective assistance; and (4) the lower court's findings that defendant committed the murder in an especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel manner and that he posed a continuing threat were supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's application for a writ of certiorari and affirmed his conviction and the sentence imposed.

 

806 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Priddy v. City of Tulsa


No. M 93-1263


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 63; 882 P.2d 81; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 71; 65 O.B.A.J. 3261



September 26, 1994, Decided  
September 26, 1994, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the Municipal Court of the City of Tulsa (Oklahoma), which convicted him of failing to have a license to engage in the business of a sign contractor in violation of Tulsa City, Okla., Ordinance tit. 51, § 2906.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of painting without having a license in violation of § 2906.1. Defendant appealed the conviction arguing that the city ordinance was unconstitutional. The court agreed and reversed the conviction. The court held that § 2906.1, as it applied to sign painters, was unconstitutional. Further, the court held that Tulsa City, Okla., Ordinance tit. 51, § 201.0 as it applied to sign painters was unconstitutional and Tulsa City, Okla., Ordinance tit. 51, § 2901.5, insofar as it required a license for sign painters in addition to a permit was unconstitutional. The court held while the city had authority to establish license requirements, there had to be an obvious and real connection between the requirements and its purpose of protecting the public welfare. The court found that the city could not justify how requiring a sign painter to have both a license and permit enhanced the public welfare. The right to acquire the means of supporting life by honest labor and skill was an inherent right of a citizen. The court found that the vocation of painting signs did not imply any sinister influence on the public calling for municipal surveillance in the form of a license.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction.

Long v. State


No. F-87-923


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 60; 883 P.2d 167; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 68; 65 O.B.A.J. 3072



September 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MUSKOGEE COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE WILLIAM H. BLISS, DISTRICT JUDGE

Original Opinion of March 23, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 18.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and Sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma) convicting defendant of two counts of first degree murder and imposing a death penalty for each count.


OVERVIEW: In rejecting defendant's claim that his confession was involuntary, the court found no evidence that defendant was misled into believing that an investigator was "on his side." The court also found that defendant knowingly and voluntarily waived his previously asserted right to silence when he initiated further conversation with the police and indicated a willingness and desire for further discussion about the investigation. The admission of certain irrelevant and prejudicial evidence did not contribute to the verdict or sentence and was, therefore, harmless error. Defendant affirmatively, voluntarily, and knowingly waived his Fifth and Sixth Amendment rights which otherwise barred the use of evidence obtained in his competency hearing. The court rejected defendant's challenges to the second-stage jury instructions addressing both aggravating and mitigating circumstances. Given the strong evidence against defendant, the prosecutor's improper appeal to religious bias in the jurors was harmless error. The sentence met the tests set forth in the court's mandatory sentence review required by Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13(C) (Supp. 1985).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and sentence on each count of first degree murder.

BARTELL v. State


Case No. F-90-0060


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 59; 881 P.2d 92; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 66; 65 O.B.A.J. 2910



September 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 11, 1994. Released for Publication October 11, 1994. As Corrected December 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RICHARD FREEMAN, DISTRICT JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which, based upon a jury's verdict and recommendation, convicted him of forcible oral sodomy of a three-year-old child and sentenced him to 13 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not question that the child had been sodomized. He introduced evidence that he did not commit the act, pointed to another possible culprit, and denied being the perpetrator. Defendant argued, in part, that he was denied his Sixth Amendment right of confrontation when a videotaped interview between the child and a detective was played for the jury and that the trial court erred in allowing the jury to hear testimony and see demonstrations using anatomically correct dolls because the evidence did not meet the Frye standard for scientific reliability. Affirming the judgment, the court held that the harmless-error analysis applied to constitutional errors in the trial process, as opposed to structural defects that affected the framework within which a trial proceeded. The court found that admission of the videotape was a trial error and that it was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, given the overwhelming properly admitted evidence that defendant was the culprit. The court determined that the dolls were demonstrative, not scientific, evidence because they were offered for illustrative purposes only and that they possessed the required degree of representational accuracy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Parker v. State


No. F-88-365


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 56; 887 P.2d 290; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 63; 65 O.B.A.J. 2809



August 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel amended September 13, 1994. Rehearing Granted December 28, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 97. Released for Publication December 28, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SEMINOLE COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE LEE STILWELL, ASSOCIATE DISTRICT JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, after a jury trial, from the District Court of Seminole County (Oklahoma) for first degree murder and his sentence to death.


OVERVIEW: The victim did not pay defendant money owed under a property contract, leading to foreclosure proceedings. The victim was shot five times. Remanding for resentencing, the court said that reversible error occurred when the trial court did not instruct the jury on all sentencing options. Life without parole was available. The trial court committed reversible error when it did not consider that option, notwithstanding the fact that the statute for the option did not become effective until after the date of the crime. Affirming the conviction, the court said that any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The trial court properly refused to move the trial. Defendant did not show prejudice by clear and convincing evidence to justify reversing the denial of a motion for a change of venue. A fair jury was selected. Defendant failed to show that the selection process had been tainted by media coverage. Ample evidence supported a finding that an arrest had been properly grounded in probable cause. The court did not agree that counsel was ineffective for failing to move for the suppression of the arrest and its effects.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding. The court affirmed the conviction.

 

810 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Canady v. Reynolds


Case No. O-94-308, Case No. O-94-309


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 54; 880 P.2d 391; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 61; 65 O.B.A.J. 2820



August 24, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OPINION ANSWERING CERTIFIED QUESTION OF LAW



DISPOSITION: QUESTION ANSWERED. RELIEF IS AVAILABLE IN STATE COURTS, BUT NOT IN THE FORMAT SOUGHT BY PETITIONERS. SPECIFICALLY WE HOLD: (1) MANDAMUS PROVIDES A VEHICLE FOR INMATES TO ENSURE DUE PROCESS IS PROVIDED WITHIN THE DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS DISCIPLINARY SYSTEM; (2) STATE LAW DOES NOT PROVIDE AN APPEAL FROM DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS ACTIONS ON DISCIPLINE; (3) HABEAS CORPUS IS THE PLENARY REMEDY FOR AN INMATE TO ADJUDICATE A RIGHT TO RELEASE BASED ON THE AMOUNT OF TIME SERVED COUPLED WITH THE NET EARNED CREDITS AWARDED; AND (4) CONSEQUENTLY, A STATE REMEDY IS AFFORDED, BUT NOT AT THE TIME THE PETITIONERS SEEK TO PREMATURELY LITIGATE THE ISSUE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmates filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus against respondent departments alleging that they were entitled to receive certain sentence credits. The District Court Judge for the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Oklahoma certified the question pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 20, §§ 1601-1611.


OVERVIEW: The inmates filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus against the departments alleging that they were entitled to receive certain sentence credits. The question was certified to the court pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 20, §§ 1601-1611. Upon review, the court determined that mandamus provided a vehicle for inmates to ensure due process was provided within the department disciplinary system. Further, the court determined that habeas corpus was the plenary remedy for the inmates to adjudicate a right to release based on the amount of time served coupled with the net earned credits awarded. Additionally, the court determined that Okla. Stat. tit. 75, § 250.4, provided a specific exception to the general rule mandating judicial review of administrative appeals, which exception excluded judicial review of an administrative decision by the departments to grant or revoke earned credits. Therefore, the court held that state law did not provide an appeal from the departments' actions on discipline.


OUTCOME: The court held that state law did not provide an appeal from the departments' actions on discipline.

Carter v. State


No. F-91-160


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 49; 879 P.2d 1234; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 57; 65 O.B.A.J. 2706



July 29, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 21, 1994. Released for Publication September 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JACK R. PARR, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which had convicted him of first degree murder while in the commission of a robbery pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981) and imposed the death penalty. He challenged numerous aspects of his trial and sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a codefendant were both found guilty of first degree murder in a joint trial at which the codefendant was sentenced to life imprisonment. The murder was committed at an auto auction where defendant had previously been employed as a security guard. The court found that: (1) the trial judge had not been biased and it had been proper to deny separate trials where defendant and his codefendant's defenses had not been mutually antagonistic where neither party inculpated the other in the murder; (2) the jury selection had been proper and it had not been error to require defendant and his codefendant to share peremptory challenges; (3) no reversible error had been committed at trial and the evidence was sufficient to convict where direct evidence existed based on defendant's admissions that he had killed a man and the fact that defendant possessed the stolen property; (4) the sentencing had been proper and none of the grounds for challenging the imposition of the death penalty were held to have merit; and (5) the prosecution was not guilty of misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for first degree murder and the resulting imposition of the death penalty.

Hogan v. State


No. F-88-918


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 41; 877 P.2d 1157; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 54; 65 O.B.A.J. 2718



July 27, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of June 8, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 44.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a rehearing of the appeals court's prior judgment in which it affirmed petitioner's conviction.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner sought a rehearing on issues raised in his appeal of his conviction. The court denied the petition. The court held that a jury instruction on the crime of manslaughter in the first degree as a lesser-included offense was not required. Because the jury was instructed and given a lesser-included offense option, the petitioner's claim failed. The court also refused to find that the aggravating circumstance "heinous, atrocious, or cruel" was unconstitutionally vague on its face. The court refused to reassess its prior holdings.


OUTCOME: The petition for rehearing was denied.

Mayes v. State


Case No. F-90-776


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 44; 887 P.2d 1288; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 48; 65 O.B.A.J. 2245



June 24, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 4, 1994. Rehearing Denied August 4, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY. THE HONORABLE GEORGE W. LINDLEY, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court, Jefferson County (Oklahoma), convicting him of murder in the first degree, conspiracy to commit murder, and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree and conspiracy to commit murder, and he was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in denying him a change of venue. The court ruled that mere publicity by itself did not establish defendant did not receive a fair trial. Further, the court held that the presumption was that defendant could receive a fair trial within the county in which he was charged and that defendant must rebut this presumption by clear and convincing evidence not only that the jurors were exposed to pretrial publicity, but also that he was prejudiced by it as a result. The court affirmed the judgment convicting and sentencing defendant, concluding that defendant presented no evidence to indicate that his right to a fair trial was interfered with and that a fair jury did not necessarily require totally uninformed jurors.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting and sentencing defendant was affirmed.

 

814 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Malone v. State


No. F-90-809


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 43; 876 P.2d 707; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 47; 65 O.B.A.J. 2161



June 17, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CARTER COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOHN SCAGGS, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Judgment is AFFIRMED and the Sentence is MODIFIED to LIFE IMPRISONMENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of murder in the first degree under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1989) and his death sentence from the District Court of Carter County (Oklahoma).


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot at several men, and killed one, when they denied that defendant's daughter lived at her home. The jury convicted defendant of first degree murder and sentenced him to death after finding two aggravating circumstances, that defendant posed a continuing threat to society and that he knowingly created a great risk of death to more than one person. On appeal, the court upheld defendant's murder conviction. However, as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13(C) (1987), the court considered whether the death sentence was imposed under any arbitrary factor and whether the evidence supported the jury's finding of the aggravating circumstances. Pursuant to this review, the court held that a 19-year-old information charging defendant with a shooting was insufficient evidence to uphold the "continuing threat" aggravator because such evidence, without more, failed to establish that defendant had a history of criminal conduct that was likely to continue. The court then determined that the mitigating evidence outweighed the remaining aggravating circumstance. Accordingly, the court vacated defendant's death sentence and modified his penalty to life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of murder in the first degree but modified his sentence from death to life imprisonment.

 

815 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State v. Humdy


No. S-93-551


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 35; 875 P.2d 429; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 42; 65 O.B.A.J. 1874



May 25, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CARTER COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ROBERT M. HIGHSMITH, ASSOCIATE DISTRICT JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged an order of the District Court of Carter County (Oklahoma) that sustained defendant's objection as to the State's intent, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1175.2(B)(3) (1981), to require defendant to testify at the pre-trial hearing that was held to determine if defendant was competent to stand trial as to the criminal charges that the State filed against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's objection was sustained on the bases that tit. 22, § 1175.2(B)(3) was unconstitutional on its face and as applied that Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1175(4)(D) (1981) also unconstitutionally violated defendant's right against self-incrimination because tit. 22, § 1175(4)(D) only provided for use immunity. The court reversed the order that sustained defendant's objection and remanded for further proceedings that were consistent with the court's opinion. Although Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1175.5 et seq. (1981) were civil in nature, the Fifth Amendment right against compulsory self-incrimination extended to both criminal and civil proceedings. However, the 1985 amendment, which allowed using a statement of a person who was found to have competent at the time of his or her examination hearing for impeachment purposes, to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1175.4(D) (1981) had the fatal constitutional flaw of not leaving an accused and the State in substantially the same positions as if the accused had claimed the Fifth Amendment privilege. The court ordered the severance of that unconstitutional clause from the rest of tit. 22, § 1175.4(D).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that sustained defendant's objection to the State's intent to call defendant to testify at the pre-trial hearing that was held to determine defendant's competency to stand trial as to the criminal charges that the State filed against him.

 

816 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bryson v. State


No. F-89-278


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 32; 876 P.2d 240; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 39; 65 O.B.A.J. 1951



May 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 5, 1994. Released for Publication July 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CHARLES L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of murder in the first degree, Okla. Stat. Tit. 21, § 701.7 (1982); third degree arson, Okla. Stat. Tit. 21, § 1493(A)(1981); solicitation to commit murder, Okla. Stat. Tit. 21, §§ 701.7, 701.6; and conspiracy to commit murder, Okla. Stat. Tit. 21, §§ 421, 701.7.


OVERVIEW: The evidence indicated that defendant and the victim's wife plotted to kill the victim. Defendant and a co-defendant beat the victim at the victim's home and then took him, in his truck to a remote location. They then set the victim and his truck on fire. The court rejected defendant's contention that the trial court erred in denying his repeated requests for a trial separate from that of his co-defendant. The court concluded that defendant's defense was not mutually antagonistic with that of his co-defendant because defendant did not attempt to exculpate himself by inculpating his co-defendant. The court also rejected defendant's contention that he was denied effective assistance of counsel by counsel's failure to present evidence crucial to his defense. Specifically, defendant contended that defense counsel failed to deliver on her opening statement promise of producing evidence to show that the victim's wife had solicited other young men to kill her husband. The court concluded that it could not say that defense counsel's decision not to call the individuals was not a tactical decision, professionally reasonable under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder in the first degree, third degree arson, solicitation to commit murder, and conspiracy to commit murder.

 

817 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Price v. State


No. F-90-554


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 26; 873 P.2d 1049; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 33; 65 O.B.A.J. 1569



April 28, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MUSKOGEE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE LYLE BURRIS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: By this Opinion on Review, Price's Judgment and Sentence for Incitement to Riot are REVERSED and the cause is REMANDED for NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma) convicted defendant of incitement to riot in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1320.2 (1981). The Emergency Appellate Division Panel No. 20 affirmed the conviction. Defendant filed a petition for review, challenging the constitutionality of § 1320.2.


OVERVIEW: The court granted review to settle to constitutional question, withdrew the Panel's opinion, and issued its opinion in place of the Panel's opinion. The court found that the case arose when two white police officers went to a housing project to arrest two black males for an unrelated offense. The court noted that a crowd gathered at the site of the arrest and defendant began speaking to the crowd, using profanity, telling the officers they were unwelcome, and urging the officers to leave. The court found that defendant was arrested after he raised a clenched fist at the officers. The court noted that the trial court did not consider the evidence in light of the clear and present danger test and refused to give defendant's requested instruction on constitutionally protected speech. The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial, holding that in each prosecution under the anti-riot statute, the trial court was required to instruct the jury that they had to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant's conduct created a clear and present danger of imminent unlawful action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for incitement to riot and remanded the matter for a new trial.

 

818 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Revilla v. State


No. F-87-993


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 24; 877 P.2d 1143; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 28; 65 O.B.A.J. 1491



April 22, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF JACKSON COUNTY. THE HONORABLE PAUL C. BRAUN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the District Court of Jackson County (Oklahoma), which convicted him for the crime of murder in the first degree, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981), and sentenced him to death. Appellant was accused of child abuse murder in the death of his girlfriend's 13-month-old son.


OVERVIEW: The child died from extensive injuries incurred while in appellant's care. Appellant claimed that the injuries were accidentally incurred. On appeal, the court held that (1) a juror was properly dismissed because voir dire showed she could not consider the death penalty; (2) the information clearly charged child abuse murder rather than first-degree malice aforethought murder where it omitted any reference to malice aforethought; (3) jury instructions adequately informed them of the State's burden to prove that the death was intentional to convict appellant under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981), and the evidence did not warrant instructions on second-degree murder, second-degree manslaughter, or misdemeanor-manslaughter; (4) testimony regarding prior abuse of the victim established the necessary requirements for child abuse and although it may have consisted of evidence of other crimes, it was properly admissible at trial; and (5) the State's provision of a list of witnesses and a detailed list of evidence to show aggravating circumstances complied with Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.10 (1981) even though it did not specify the witness that would testify to particular bad acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

819 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Duvall v. State


Case No. PC-93-644


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 19; 871 P.2d 1386; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 25; 65 O.B.A.J. 1202



March 28, 1994, Decided  
March 28, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Opinion of February 10, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 11.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant in an Oklahoma death penalty case sought reconsideration of the dismissal of his application for post-conviction relief, and requested reinstatement of his appeal and a stay of execution.


OVERVIEW: Following the court's order dismissing defendant's application for post-conviction relief, defendant moved for reconsideration. He argued that the court in its order misstated the procedural history of the case, that he was not required to file a Petition in Error, that his appeal could not be dismissed because of his failure to file a petition in error, that the requirement to do so amounted to an unconstitutionally vague requirement denying him due process of law, and that his appeal was dismissed on a technicality. The court disagreed. It held that a Petition in Error was required to confirm jurisdiction for appeal under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1087. In addition, defendant had both the time originally allotted and three extensions of time in which to present the court with the record it needed to obtain jurisdiction and adjudicate his appeal. He failed to do so. Therefore he had defaulted on his right to have his post-conviction appeal heard by the court. His motion for reconsideration and stay of execution was denied.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion was denied. The court found that defendant had the proper time allotted to him on appeal plus three extensions. By failing to accomplish his appeal within the time provided, he had defaulted on his right to have his post-conviction appeal heard.

 

820 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. State


Case No. F-89-549


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 13; 871 P.2d 79; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13; 65 O.B.A.J. 675



February 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE BANA BLASDEL, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: The Judgment and sentence for First Degree Murder is AFFIRMED; the judgment and sentence for Felonious Possession of a Firearm is REVERSED and REMANDED for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted her of murder in the first degree and possession of a firearm after former conviction of a felony. The jury found the existence of two aggravating circumstances and recommended death as punishment for murder and 10 years for felonious possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant killed her girlfriend because she was leaving her. The shooting happened after defendant and her girlfriend argued, where defendant then followed the victim to the police station. Among many contentions of error, defendant claimed that she was improperly denied jury instructions on a self-defense theory. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and death sentence, holding that defendant was not entitled to such an instruction under the facts shown. The court noted that even if the victim was the initial aggressor she clearly indicated a desire to withdraw. Also, when defendant followed the victim she became the pursuer, which was clear when she retrieved a gun to shoot the girlfriend. Thus, the evidence did not support the request for a self-defense instruction. The court remanded on the sentence for the firearm charge because due to an error in the jury instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence of death for first degree murder. The court reversed the judgment and sentence for felonious possession of a firearm and remanded for a new trial.

 

821 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


Case No. F-89-22


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 12; 871 P.2d 56; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 14; 65 O.B.A.J. 691



February 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GRADY COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JAMES R. WINCHESTER, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Grady County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of murder in the first degree and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the venue, jury selection, insufficiency of evidence of premeditation, admission of opinion evidence, jury charges, prosecutorial misconduct, competency of counsel, defendant's absence from the sentencing, and the constitutionality of the aggravating factor of a continuing threat to society. The court affirmed. Defendant failed to show prejudice from the venue or from any incompetent assistance of counsel. Defendant failed to prove a fair-cross section violation or an abuse of discretion in the jury selection. The physical evidence belied an absence of premeditation. The opinion of an investigator as to where the victim was standing when shot by defendant was admissible as testimony helpful to the trier of fact. No reversible error resulted from prosecutorial misconduct. The record showed that defendant validly waived his right to be present at sentencing. The challenged aggravator was constitutional. As to jury instructions, defendant underestimated severely the ability of the jury to determine which instructions applied to the first stage and the second stage of the proceedings. Defendant's remaining contentions lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

822 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ballard


Case No. S-91-769


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 6; 868 P.2d 738; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 7; 65 O.B.A.J. 560



February 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL ON A RESERVE QUESTION OF LAW FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMANCHE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JACK BROCK, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision from the District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma), which pronounced that Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-503.2 was unconstitutional following defendant's conviction for four drug-related offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea and was convicted for four drug-related counts. The trial court entered a notation on the judgment and sentences that Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-503.2 (Supp. 1990) was unconstitutional. The State asserted that the statute was constitutional. The court reversed the determination that the statute was unconstitutional and remanded the case for further proceedings regarding sentencing. The court held that: (1) the statute did not deny equal protection because there was a rational basis in imposing an additional assessment on those convicted of drug-related crimes and use of that money to go towards educating and helping others who may have or are likely to become involved with controlled dangerous substances; (2) the statute did not deny equal protection to indigents because the assessment was a cost that operated like any other cost of a criminal proceeding that operated only to make the indigent a judgment debtor; (3) the astute provided adequate guidance in the range of fees to be assessed; and (4) the statute did not improperly shift the tax gathering responsibility to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision from the trial court.

 

823 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State v. Claborn


Case No. S-92-164


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 8; 870 P.2d 169; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 15; 65 O.B.A.J. 668



February 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL ON A RESERVED QUESTION OF LAW FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF JOHNSTON COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOHN H. SCAGGS, DISTRICT JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of the District Court of Johnston County (Oklahoma), which declared Okla. Stat. tit. 20, § 1313.2(B) (1988), Okla. Stat. tit. 20 § 1313.2(A) (1990), and Okla. Stat. Supp. tit. 21, § 142.18 (1990) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a judgment declaring the statutory assessments unconstitutional and the State appealed. The court held that the statutes at issue were not violative of the separation of powers doctrine. The court found that the various assessments were reasonably related to the costs of administering the criminal justice system and were not simply an executive branch "tax." Further, the court found that the statutory assessments were properly enacted by the legislature in its role as lawmaker. The court found that their enactment did not infringe upon matters within the exclusive province of the judiciary. The court further held that the assessments did not violate the free access to courts provision in Okla. Const. art. II, § 6 nor the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order declaring the statutory assessments unconstitutional.

 

824 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. S-90-1067


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1992 OK CR 72; 877 P.2d 1136; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 4; 65 O.B.A.J. 471



January 26, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MUSKOGEE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM H. BLISS, DISTRICT JUDGE

Original Opinion of October 29, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 90.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendants petitioned for a rehearing of the court's previous opinion, which reversed a judgment holding that Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 1503(C)(1) (Supp. 1988) was unconstitutionally vague and invalid and remanded the case for trial.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed the trial court's ruling pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1053.1 (1981). The court reversed and remanded for trial. Defendants petitioned for rehearing and argued that further prosecution was barred because the effect of the trial court's ruling was the same as that of an order sustaining a demurrer to an information. The court held that: (1) the precedent upon which defendants relied was inapplicable because it related to a judgment that had been rendered before the effective date of § 1053.1, which provided for an automatic appeal of judgments holding statutes unconstitutional in criminal cases; (2) an erroneous judgment holding a statute to be unconstitutional was not tantamount to one sustaining a demurrer to an information where the defects as enumerated in Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 504 (1991) appeared on the face of the information or where there was insufficient evidence; (3) the effect of an appeal under § 1053.1 did not bar further prosecution except where there had been a trial on the merits before a judge who subsequently ruled a statute unconstitutional; and (4) State v. Tinkler, 815. P. 2d 190 (Okla. Crim. App. 1991) was expressly overruled.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for trial as per its original opinion.

 

825 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Ellis v. State


No. F-86-887


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1992 OK CR 45; 867 P.2d 1289; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5; 65 O.B.A.J. 475



January 26, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. THE HONORABLE RAYMOND NAIFEH, DISTRICT JUDGE

Original Opinion of July 24, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 62.



DISPOSITION: After further reconsideration, we again AFFIRM the Judgments and Sentences, and appellant's request for relief is DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a rehearing of the court's decision that affirmed defendant's convictions for murder in the first degree and shooting with intent to kill. Defendant was sentenced to death for each of the three murder counts, and he was sentenced to thousands of years imprisonment for the shooting with intent to kill convictions.


OVERVIEW: The court found that a few of defendant's allegations of error were appropriate for rehearing, and the review was limited to those issues. Defendant first argued that comments made by a district attorney, who incorrectly stated that defendant voluntarily committed himself to a hospital, denied him a fair trial and reliable sentencing hearing. The court found, however, that after reviewing for fundamental error, the comments did not deprive defendant of a fair trial because the misstatements were not so egregious so as to amount to fundamental error that would require reversal or modification. The court next found that there was no error in the trial court's decision to not declare a mistrial following an emotional outburst in the courtroom because the incident was of short duration and the trial court took appropriate measures to prevent unfair prejudice. Finally, the court found that, although a more thorough account of the mitigating evidence was necessary, the sentences of death were factually substantiated and appropriate because it was clear that the jury's improper consideration of an unconstitutional aggravator did not play a significant role in the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The court again affirmed the judgments and sentences, and defendant's request for relief was denied.

PAXTON v. STATE


No. F-89-1199


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1993 OK CR 59; 867 P.2d 1309; 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 64; 65 O.B.A.J. 120



December 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 10, 1994.
Rehearing denied by, 02/10/1994
Writ of certiorari denied Paxton v. Oklahoma, 513 U.S. 886, 115 S. Ct. 227, 130 L. Ed. 2d 153, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 6534 (Oct. 3, 1994)
Post-conviction relief denied at Paxton v. State, 1996 OK CR 4, 910 P.2d 1059, 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5 (Okla. Crim. App., Jan. 12, 1996)

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) convicting him of murder, and possession of a firearm after former conviction of a felony, and sentencing appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant arrived at the home of decedent. When she answered the door, appellant shot and killed her. As a result of his actions, appellant was convicted of murder, and possession of a firearm after former conviction of a felony, and was sentenced to death. ROBEDEAUX v. STATE


No. F-86-463


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1993 OK CR 57; 866 P.2d 417; 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 63; 65 O.B.A.J. 58



December 20, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 10, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RAYMOND NAIFEH, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) convicting him of first-degree murder, and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant shared an apartment with his girlfriend, the victim. The tenants below appellant's apartment reported hearing loud noises from the apartment, and then never seeing the victim again. Thereafter, pieces of the victim began to surface all over the county. Appellant was charged with murdering the victim, and was eventually convicted of the crime and sentenced to death. Appellant challenged the conviction and sentence raising numerous points of error. Of the most important alleged errors raised by appellant was a challenge to the sufficiency of the information under which he was charged. Specifically, appellant argued that it was insufficient because it failed to state what body parts were found of the victim, and what weapon was used. The court held that appellant was properly placed on notice of the relevant criminal offense and the circumstances surrounding its commission. Therefore, the information was deemed sufficient. As to appellant's remaining contentions, the court found that they were without merit, and affirmed both the conviction and the death sentence.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Salazar v. State


Case No. F-88-569


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1993 OK CR 39; 859 P.2d 517; 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 44; 64 O.B.A.J. 2604



August 30, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Opinion of April 29, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 24.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Comanche County District Court (Oklahoma), which convicted him of the crimes of first degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1982) and first degree burglary in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1431 (1981). The court vacated his sentence of death for his murder conviction and remanded the cause for resentencing. The State sought a rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the crimes of first degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1982) and first degree burglary in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1431 (1981). The jury set punishment on the burglary conviction at 10 years imprisonment. Following a second stage proceeding, the jury recommended defendant be put to death for the murder conviction. The trial court sentenced accordingly and defendant appealed to the court. The court affirmed defendant's judgment and sentence for first degree burglary. Defendant's conviction for first degree murder was also affirmed, but his sentence of death was vacated and the cause remanded for resentencing. The State filed a petition for rehearing. The court denied the State's petition. The court rejected the State's argument that an amendment to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 701.10a (1991) warranted a rehearing of the case. To have applied § 701.10a to defendant would have deprived him of a sentencing option and would have resulted in harsher penalty options, which would have violated the prohibition against imposing a harsher punishment in an ex post facto manner.


OUTCOME: The court denied the State's petition for a rehearing after the court remanded the cause for resentencing of defendant's murder conviction.

Trice v. State


NO. F-87-573


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1993 OK CR 19; 853 P.2d 203; 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 22; 64 O.B.A.J. 1285



April 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 14, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM R. BURKETT, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first-degree malice aforethought murder, first-degree rape, first-degree burglary, and assault and battery with a dangerous weapon. The jury found four aggravating circumstances and sentenced appellant to death on the first-degree murder count and 999 years imprisonment for each of the non-capital counts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raped and savagely bludgeoned to death an 84-year-old woman, and he beat her mentally retarded son so severely that he eventually lost an eye. Defendant fled with $ 300 that he used to buy drugs. Defendant failed to establish that the use of the voter registration list to compose the jury panel or an exemption of voters age 70 or older violated the fair-cross-section requirement or that the trial court abused its discretion in excusing jurors that could not consider the death penalty. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting photographs of the murder victim taken at the crime scene, and the opinion testimony of an officer regarding a comparison of defendant's shoe print with one found at the crime scene was properly admitted. Although the "heinous, atrocious, or cruel" aggravating circumstance instruction was unconstitutionally vague, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, finding that the jury's consideration of the aggravator was at most harmless error. The sentence of death was factually substantiated and appropriate considering the three remaining valid aggravating circumstances as well as the mitigating evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Long v. State


No. F-87-923


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 18; 64 O.B.A.J. 1005



March 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Opinion of September 14, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 68.
 [*1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MUSKOGEE COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE WILLIAM H. BLISS, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of two counts of murder in the first degree and sentenced defendant to death for each count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed a victim 31 times, twice breaking off pieces of a knife blade in her body, and shot her in the head and abdomen. He then shot her four-year-old son twice at point blank range and stabbed him. On appeal, the court held that there was no error warranting reversal or modification. The court found there was nothing coercive in the police treatment of defendant and found no evidence that the statement was not voluntary within the meaning of the Due Process Clause. Although the State conceded that no notice was given to defendant of the evidence to be used in the second stage of the trial, the court found that the omission was both harmless and waived. The court held that defendant affirmatively, voluntarily, and knowingly waived his Fifth and Sixth Amendment rights, which might have barred the use of evidence obtained in a competency hearing, because defendant did not object to the testimony and the defense cross-examined the witness. The court found that the facts were sufficient for any rational trier of fact to find defendant inflicted serious physical abuse on the first victim, and that the prosecutor's improper appeal to religious bias in the jurors was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

831 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


WOODRUFF v. STATE


No. F-87-442


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1993 OK CR 7; 846 P.2d 1124; 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 10; 64 O.B.A.J. 166



January 13, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM SAIED, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence by the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) for murder in the first degree in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981) and robbery with a dangerous weapon after former conviction of a felony in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 801 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's charges on two murders were tried separately. The State raised the subject murder in the sentencing phase of the first murder trial. That conviction was overturned. During the sentencing phase on the subject murder, the State raised defendant's first murder. Defendant claimed that because the murder was raised in the first murder trial, he could not have been prosecuted on the subject murder charge. The court held that the conviction was supported by sufficient, though conflicting and circumstantial, evidence and that the sentences were proper. The murder charge was not collaterally estopped or barred by double jeopardy when it was raised during the first murder trial because that was not an independent crime, it was not an adjudication, and the first murder was relevant to determine a proper sentence. Thus, the first murder was relevant to prove defendant's propensity to commit future violent crimes. However, the murder should not have been raised as proof of a prior felony because it was overturned. However, that error was harmless because it was cumulative. The jury was not overly prejudiced by the disclosure of the first murder to determine the sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentences.

 

832 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


ROMANO v. STATE


No. F-87-441


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1993 OK CR 8; 847 P.2d 368; 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 11; 64 O.B.A.J. 150



January 13, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM SAIED, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of murder in the first degree, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7, and robbery with a dangerous weapon, after former conviction of two or more felonies, in violation of § 801. The jury found four aggravating circumstances and recommended punishment of death. The trial court sentenced accordingly.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's body was discovered in his apartment. The decedent had been beaten, strangled, and stabbed. The court found no reversible error in jury selection. The mere fact that one juror knew the victim's daughter did not render him incapable of serving on the jury. Defense counsel's failure to remove that juror was a part of trial strategy and was not ineffective assistance. Two prospective jurors were not improperly removed from the panel because their views about capital punishment would have prevented or substantially impaired their duties as jurors in accordance with the instructions and their oath. No violation of equal protection principles arose. The court also held that the evidence was sufficient and that the prosecutor's comments did not deprive defendant of a fair trial. The verdicts rendered in accordance with Oklahoma's capital sentencing procedure were general verdicts that complied with the requirements of Okla. Const. art. 7, § 15. The court held that defendant's prior felony convictions and the violent manner in which the robbery was committed supported the sentence. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's finding of aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence.

 

833 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


WALTERS v. STATE


No. F-88-0643


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1993 OK CR 4; 848 P.2d 20; 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5; 64 O.B.A.J. 86



January 11, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 6, 1993. Released for Publication April 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE JAY D. DALTON, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Judgment and Sentence is AFFIRMED except for the Crime Victim's Compensation assessment which is VACATED AND REMANDED to the trial court for proper hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of injury to minor child after former conviction, a violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 843, and sentenced him to 25 years imprisonment. The court also made a crime victims compensation assessment pursuant to the Crime Victims Compensation Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 142.1 et seq. (1984).


OVERVIEW: At sentencing, the trial court added an assessment of $ 10,000 to the Victim's Compensation Fund pursuant to the Act. Defendant challenged the assessment, among other things, contending that the sentencing procedure violated his rights to due process. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence but reversed the crime victims compensation assessment on the ground that the trial court did not consider all of the factors mandated by Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 142.18(A) (1984). The court reasoned that although ample evidence was presented at trial as to the severity of the crime and defendant's prior criminal record, no evidence was presented at trial or the sentencing hearing regarding defendant's ability to pay, or the economic impact of the assessment on defendant's dependents. The court determined that this lack of evidence constituted reversible error because it was the consideration of these four facts that satisfied the due process requirement that the assessment was not arbitrary. The court also decided that it could not presume the statutorily required elements were considered where no evidence in the record addressed them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, but reversed the imposition of the crime victims compensation assessment and remanded with instructions to the trial court to conduct a complete hearing as contemplated by the Act.

 

834 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. State


No. PC-89-42


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1992 OK CR 79; 845 P.2d 1272; 1992 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 97; 63 O.B.A.J. 3655



December 1, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JACK R. PARR, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment from the District Court, in Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which denied his application for postconviction relief. The inmate had previously been convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The court affirmed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The inmate made many allegations of error that were never raised at trial or on direct appeal of his conviction. He argued that exculpatory evidence material to the case was not disclosed to him. He also asserted that his death sentence violated the eighth and fourteenth amendments because the "heinous, atrocious, or cruel" aggravating circumstance in the instruction was applied in an unconstitutionally vague and overbroad manner, and further because the evidence was insufficient to support the jury's findings of that circumstance. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The allegations of error not raised at trial or on direct appeal were not properly before the court. The statement referred to as exculpatory was an unsworn prior inconsistent statement made by a co-defendant and was not exculpatory in nature. As such, it was not subject to discovery by the inmate. The jury was instructed that the aggravating circumstance was to be directed to crimes where the death of the victim was preceded by torture or serious physical abuse of the victim. That instruction was sufficient to define the aggravating circumstance and provide objective factors overcoming any vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court that denied post-conviction relief to the inmate who was convicted for first-degree murder and sentenced to death.

 

835 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Okla. v. Johnson


No. S-90-1067


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1992 OK CR 72; 877 P.2d 1136; 1992 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 90; 63 O.B.A.J. 3200



October 29, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion on Rehearing January 26, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 4.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MUSKOGEE COUNTY. HONORABLE WILLIAM H. BLISS, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged by information with selling motor vehicles or motor vehicle parts with altered identification numbers in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 1503(C)(1) (Supp. 1988). The District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma) dismissed the information on the grounds that § 1503(C)(1) was unconstitutionally vague and invalid. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants mounted facial constitutional challenges to Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 1503(C)(1) (Supp. 1988) on the grounds of overbreadth and vagueness. Defendants alleged that § 1503(C)(1) violated due process by making proof of one fact or group of facts evidence of the existence of the ultimate fact upon which guilt was predicated. Defendants also alleged that the State's amended information failed to properly allege a crime. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for trial. The court rejected defendant's facial overbreadth challenge to § 1503(C)(1) where defendant's conduct was constitutionally proscribed by § 1503(C)(1), and defendants' challenges were based upon hypothetical applications of § 1503 not before the court. The court held that defendants' vagueness challenge failed where a person of ordinary intelligence would be apprised that defendants' conduct was proscribed under § 1503(1). The court held that §1503(1) did not contain an unconstitutional presumption and that the information adequately stated a violation of § 1503(C)(1).


OUTCOME: The court revered the judgment of the trial court and remanded for trial.

State ex rel. Moss v. Couch


No. S-91-98


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1992 OK CR 66; 841 P.2d 1154; 1992 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 82; 1 Wage & Hour Cas. 2d (BNA) 294; 63 O.B.A.J. 2943

October 5, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] This Opinion is Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of September 8, 1992, Reported at 1992 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 76.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order of a magistrate sustaining defendant's demurrer to the information and dismissing the State's case against defendant from the Tulsa County District Court (Oklahoma) after the magistrate found that the statute under which defendant was charged, Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 165.8 (1981), was unconstitutional because it set up what amounted to be a debtor's prison and made doing a civil wrong a criminal offense.


OVERVIEW: An employee of defendant filed a wage claim form with the Oklahoma State Department of Labor seeking to recover unpaid wages from defendant. After defendant failed to respond, the Department forwarded the matter to the Tulsa County District Attorney's office for criminal prosecution under Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 165.2, for the claim of non-payment of wages. The State charged defendant with the crime of failure to pay wages. In affirming the magistrate's dismissal of the case, the court found that the prosecution violated Okla. Const. art. II, § 13, which prohibited imprisonment for debt. Defendant had been charged with, and prosecuted for, the existence of a debt arising out of contract and the refusal to pay such debt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the magistrate's order dismissing the case from the district court.

 

837 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Clayton v. State


No. F-86-165


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1992 OK CR 60; 840 P.2d 18; 1992 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 77; 63 O.B.A.J. 2803



September 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 3, 1992. Released for Publication November 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DONALD C. LANE, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of first degree murder and upon the jury's recommendation sentenced defendant to death. Defendant claimed reversible error on a number of theories. One of the issues addressed was whether it was a denial of due process to conduct the competency hearing after the trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and raised several issues on appeal. One of the more important was whether it was an error to admit his confession after he saw his lawyer and was told not to talk to the police. Despite his attorney's advice, defendant volunteered the information after his attorney left even after being warned by the police about what his attorney had advised. The court held that the police had only asked routine booking questions after the attorney had left, and in no way improperly interrogated defendant. Having been warned by his lawyer and the police, defendant's statements were properly admitted as voluntary. Another major issue was the trial court's failure to conduct the mandatory competency hearing once defendant's possible incompetency was raised. The court held that under the particular factual circumstances the hearing was properly conducted post-trial upon remand following an earlier appeal. The court held that defendant's competency at the time of the trial was meaningfully determined at the post-trial hearing on credible and competent evidence and that any error in failing to hold the hearing at the proper time was cured.


OUTCOME: The court held that all of defendant's assignments of error were without merit and affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of first degree murder and sentenced him to death.

 

838 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Moss v. Couch


No. S-91-98


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1992 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 76; 63 O.B.A.J. 2654



September 8, 1992, Decided  
September 8, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication September 22, 1992.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the judgment of a special judge acting as a magistrate, which sustained the defendant's demurrer and dismissed his pending prosecution in Tulsa County District Court (Oklahoma) on a charge of failing to pay wages, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 165.8 (Supp. 1982). The court placed the case upon its accelerated docket.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged under § 165.8 with failing to pay accrued wages as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 165.2 (Supp. 1982). The special trial judge sustained his demurrer on a finding that Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 165.8 (Supp. 1982) was unconstitutional because it made it a criminal offense for committing a civil wrong. On appeal, the State argued that § 165.8 was not unconstitutional. In affirming, the court found that violations of Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 165.2 (Supp. 1982) were designated as misdemeanors pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 165.8 (Supp. 1982) and were punishable by fine and imprisonment pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 10 (1981). The court held that such treatment of the failure to pay wages was contrary to Okla. Const. art. II, § 13, which prohibited imprisonment for debt and that no distinction was made for the honest employer who became economically unable to pay wages that were due and owing. The court noted that it was disinclined to hold that § 13 prohibited all criminal prosecutions for violations of Okla. Stat. tit. 40, §§ 165.1 through 165.11 (Supp. 1982) but did so hold for prosecutions for violations of Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 165.2 (Supp. 1982).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial judge's order of dismissal.

Ellis v. State


No. F-86-887


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1992 OK CR 45; 867 P.2d 1289; 1992 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 62; 63 O.B.A.J. 2327



July 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion on Rehearing January 26, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5. Rehearing Denied January 26, 1994. Released for Publication January 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. THE HONORABLE RAYMOND NAIFEH, DISTRICT JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions by the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) for three counts of murder in the first degree and four counts of shooting with intent to kill. Defendant also challenged death sentence set by the jury after it found three of the aggravating circumstances enumerated in Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.12, including that the murders were heinous, atrocious or cruel, § 701.12(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not deny the acts of which he was accused, but raised the defense of insanity pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 152(4) (1981). Prior to trial, defendant was examined to determine his competence to stand trial pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1175.1 (1981). He offered records of his competency evaluation to support his insanity defense at trial but the trial court ruled that the records were irrelevant. On appeal, the court affirmed the ruling and held that the question of an accused's competency to stand trial was an entirely different matter than the defense of insanity and that any probative value of the competency evidence was substantially outweighed by the danger of misleading the jury and confusing the issues of competency and insanity. With regard, to sentencing, the court struck the aggravating circumstance of heinous, atrocious or cruel because the trial court failed to instruct the jury that the circumstance applied only to those murders in which torture or serious physical abuse preceded the victim's death. The death sentence was affirmed, however, because the jury found two other aggravating circumstances in each murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder in the first degree and shooting with intent to kill. The court also affirmed the death sentences.
