Underwood v. State


No. PC-89-1211


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1990 OK CR 1; 786 P.2d 707; 1990 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2



January 2, 1990, Decided  
January 2, 1990, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Tulsa County District Court (Oklahoma), which denied his request for postconviction relief to modify an indeterminate sentence that had been imposed following his conviction for second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of second-degree murder and imposed an indeterminate prison sentence of not less than 15 years or more than 30 years. Defendant argued that Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.9(B) (Supp. 1987) did not permit an indeterminate sentence and sought to have his sentence modified to a 15-year term. The court held that defendant's sentence was proper because Okla. Stat. tit. 57, § 353 (Supp. 1987), which was in effect when defendant was convicted and sentenced, could be used in conjunction with Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.9(B) where a jury imposed a life sentence or a minimum term in excess of one-third of the maximum term.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

883 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Doyle v. State


No. F-86-356


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1989 OK CR 85; 785 P.2d 317; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 89



December 26, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County. The Honorable Preston Trimble, District Judge. David Lee Doyle, Appellant, was tried by jury and convicted in the District Court of Cleveland County, Case No. CRF-85-423, of Robbery with a Dangerous Weapon (21 O.S. 1981, § 791), Two Counts of Kidnapping (21 O.S. 1981, § 741), and Four Counts of Forcible Sodomy (21 O.S. 1981, § 888), and Case No. CRF-85-420 of Three Counts of First Degree Rape (21 O.S. 1981, § 1114). The jury recommended as punishment twenty (20) years imprisonment for Robbery with a Dangerous Weapon, fifty (50) years imprisonment for one count of Kidnapping, thirty (30) years imprisonment for each count of Forcible Sodomy, and one hundred twenty five (125) years imprisonment for each count of First Degree Rape. The trial court sentenced accordingly. From this judgment and sentence, Appellant appeals. We AFFIRM.



DISPOSITION:  We Affirm.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of robbery with a dangerous weapon, kidnapping, sodomy, and first degree rape in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, §§ 791, 741, 888, 1114 (1981) and sentenced him to 225 years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery with a dangerous weapon, kidnapping, sodomy, and first degree rape in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, §§ 791, 741, 888, 1114 (1981). The trial court sentenced him to 225 years of imprisonment, and defendant sought review. The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2701 (1981) allowed the admission of an opinion by a lay witness if the opinion was rationally based on the perception of the witness and was helpful to a clear understanding of his testimony or the determination of a fact in issue. The court found that the Double Jeopardy prohibition against multiple punishment forbid the penalizing of defendant more severely than the law provided. The court determined that the kidnapping, rape, and sodomy statutes were separate and distinct offenses, each requiring dissimilar proof of their several elements. The court found that, merely because the crimes were committed in rapid succession did not negate the fact that separate crimes were committed, so long as separation existed. The court held that defendant's double jeopardy had not been violated and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court.

Jones v. State

1989 OK CR 66; 781 P.2d 326; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 63

DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the District Court of Seminole County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of lewd molestation in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1123 (1981).

The court concluded that the admission of the victim's hearsay statements to various people about the sexual assaults under Okla. The court held that the testimony of each witness to the victim's statements was relevant and necessary to explain the circumstances surrounding the sexual abuse. Fox v. State


No. F-86-511


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1989 OK CR 51; 779 P.2d 562; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 55



August 30, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 2, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable David M. Cook, District Judge. Billy Ray Fox, appellant, was convicted in Oklahoma County District Court of three counts of Murder in the First Degree, Case No. CRF-85-3343, and was given three sentences of the death penalty.



DISPOSITION:  Judgments and sentences are AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions by the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) for three counts of murder in the first degree while in the commission of a robbery with a dangerous weapon and his three death penalty sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his codefendant robbed a grocery store and killed three employees, one of whom was stabbed multiple times and bludgeoned. Defendant was convicted of three counts of murder in the first degree while committing a robbery with a dangerous weapon and sentenced to death on each count. On appeal, the court held that defendant's conviction was proper because (1) he was not denied a jury representing a fair cross-section of the community; (2) he did not demonstrate antagonistic defenses nor prejudice resulting from being tried with his codefendant; and (3) his incriminating statement to two officers after his arrest and request for counsel was voluntary, given that the officers advised defendant that they were not there to discuss his case, and their giving their business cards in case he or his attorney wished to contact the police did not amount to an interrogation. The court ruled that the sentences of death were proper because they were not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor, and the evidence supported the jury's findings of the four aggravating circumstances charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder in the first degree while in the commission of a robbery with a dangerous weapon and his sentences of death.

Foster v. State


Case No. PC-87-729


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1989 OK CR 50; 779 P.2d 591; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 54



August 21, 1989, Decided  
August 22, 1989, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the United States Supreme Court, the Court of Criminal Appeals (Oklahoma), addressed whether the death penalty was proper under the circumstances of defendant's case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant beat a 77-year old grocery delivery man to death and then took his body to a remote area, stabbed the body several more times, and covered the body up with leaves, sticks, and the floor-mats of his own truck. Defendant was sentenced to death. On appeal before the United States Supreme Court, the court found that defendant's death sentence was invalid because of the aggravating circumstances relied upon in that case as support for the imposition of the death penalty were unconstitutionally vague. On remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed the jury's verdict, and held that the jury's finding that the murder was "especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel" did not violate the previous dictates in Furman v. Georgia, requiring that the discretion of the sentencer be limited by some comprehensible standards. The jury was sufficiently advised of the limits to the amount of discretion which was available for exercise in the determination of whether the crime committed was "especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel" and concomitantly, whether the death penalty was the appropriate punishment. The trial court articulated the definition of each of these words.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding that the trial court had properly articulated the standards required by the United States Supreme Court in instructing the jury to consider the death penalty.

 

887 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Cartwright v. State


No. H-88-820


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1989 OK CR 41; 778 P.2d 479; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 45



July 31, 1989, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus and modification of invalid death sentence to life imprisonment after the United States Supreme Court affirmed the circuit court's order that denied a writ of habeas corpus but vacated his death sentence as invalid under the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution, and without prejudice to further proceedings in the state courts for resentencing.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that he had been deprived of a substantial right to an automatic sentence of life imprisonment when judgment vacating his death sentence was rendered without prejudice so that he could have been resentenced in the state courts. On appeal, the court remanded to the district court for resentencing pursuant to an amended sentencing statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13(E)(2) (1985), which the court held authorized remand of a capital case for resentencing. The court ruled that Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 3 (1981), which prohibited retroactive application, had not prohibited application of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13(E)(2) (Supp. 1985) on remand, and to the extent Dutton v. Dixon, 757 P.2d 376 (Okla. Crim. 1988), was inconsistent, it was expressly overruled. The court ruled that the ex post facto clause had not prevented the State from depriving a criminal defendant of an expectation as to a procedure that had not yet accrued to his benefit. Therefore, petitioner could have been resentenced under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13(E)(2) (Supp. 1985), without violating due process or the ex post facto prohibition of either the Oklahoma or federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court remanded petitioner's capital case to the district court for resentencing in accordance with an amended sentencing statute.

Dean v. State


No. F-86-94


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1989 OK CR 40; 778 P.2d 476; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 40



July 28, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Muskogee County, Oklahoma. The Honorable James E. Edmondson, District Judge. Warren Harding Dean, Appellant, was convicted of Possession of a Controlled Dangerous Substance (Marijuana) in a Penal Institution After Former Conviction of Two or More Felonies, in the District Court of Muskogee County, Case No. CRF 85-1, and sentenced to twenty (20) years imprisonment and appeals. Appellant's original conviction of Possession of a Controlled Dangerous Substance (Marijuana) in a Penal Institution and sentence of Five (5) years imprisonment is AFFIRMED. The judgment of Possession of a Controlled Dangerous Substance (Marijuana) in a Penal Institution After Former Conviction of Two or More Felonies and sentence of Twenty (20) years imprisonment is VACATED.



DISPOSITION:  The case is REMANDED to the District Court of Muskogee County with direction to enter an amended judgment and sentence consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of possession of a controlled dangerous substance in a penal institution after former conviction of two or more felonies, and which sentenced him to 20 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found to be in the possession of a baggie containing marijuana while he was an inmate. Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled dangerous substance in a penal institution after former conviction of two or more felonies, however, the jury could not agree on punishment. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a mistrial, discharged the jury, and imposed a five-year sentence. Both sides then filed motions for a new trial. The court granted the State's motion for a new trial as to the punishment stage and set the case for a jury trial. A new jury sentenced defendant to 20 years. The court held that the trial court was without authority to grant the motion for a new trial and reconvene a new jury for sentencing purposes only because there was no showing of good cause for the late presentation and the motion came too late for appropriate consideration. However, the trial court did properly exercise its authority pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 927 (1981) when it imposed the original five year sentence. The trial court properly concluded that the jury could not agree to punishment, discharged them from further deliberation, and set the punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants original conviction and sentence of five years imprisonment vacated the judgment sentencing him to 20 years, and remanded to the trial court with direction to enter an amended judgment and sentence.

 

889 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


City of Tulsa v. Martin


No. S-87-884


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1989 OK CR 24; 775 P.2d 824; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 26



June 12, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the Municipal Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Millie Otey, Municipal Judge. Petitioner, the City of Tulsa, has appealed to this Court on a reserved question of law. Respondent, Christopher Martin, was charged with a violation of Tulsa's Mandatory Seat Belt Ordinance in the Tulsa County Municipal Court, Case No. 8796034. The judge declared the ordinance under which respondent was charged unconstitutional and dismissed the case.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Tulsa, Oklahoma, sought review of an order of the Municipal Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which granted appellee motorist's motion to dismiss on the ground that the ordinance the motorist was charged with violating, Tulsa, Oklahoma, Rev. Ordinances tit. 37, § 338, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance required operators and front seat passengers of passenger cars to wear a seatbelt. The motorist had challenged the ordinance on equal protection grounds, as the ordinance exempted pickup trucks, recreational vehicles, and vans. The court noted at the outset that the Oklahoma legislature had amended the vehicle classification statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 12-417 (Supp. 1987) to remove pickup trucks and vans from the list of vehicles to which the seat belt requirement did not apply. Therefore, the remaining legislative distinction being challenged was that between passenger cars and recreational vehicles. The court held that because the distinctions in neither the ordinance nor statute were inherently invidious or impinged upon fundamental rights, the rational basis test applied to determine their constitutionality. The court concluded that the legislative distinction between passenger cars and recreational vehicles was valid under the rational basis standard. The promotion of public safety was a legitimate governmental goal, and the court could reasonably conceive of facts that would justify treating passenger cars and recreational vehicles differently.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Maxwell v. State


No. F-86-321


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1989 OK CR 22; 775 P.2d 818; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 24



May 24, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal for the District Court of Muskogee County, The Honorable Bruce Sewell, Associate District Judge. DONALD RAY MAXWELL, Appellant, was convicted by jury of Attempted Kidnapping After Former Conviction of Two or More Felonies, Case No. CRF-85-299, in the Muskogee County District Court, before the Honorable Bruce Sewell, Associate District Judge, and was sentenced to life imprisonment, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma) for attempted kidnapping after former conviction of two or more felonies and his sentence of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted kidnapping after former conviction of two or more felonies and sentenced to life imprisonment. Finding no error, the court affirmed the judgment and sentence. The declaration of a mistrial was not warranted by the detective's testimony that the victim identified defendant at the police station on the night of the crime. Because defendant did not object, the court reviewed for fundamental error only. The testimony was merely cumulative because the victim testified to the extrajudicial identification before the detective testified. Having found the admission of the detective's testimony to be harmless error, the court found that defense counsel's failure to object to it did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel. An extensive proportionality analysis was not required to determine whether defendant's sentence was excessive, in violation of the Eighth Amendment, because the sentence did not foreclose the possibility of parole. The sentence did not shock the court's conscience because there was no maximum sentence under the recidivist statute, the attempted kidnapping was violent, and defendant's prior felonies involved violence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted kidnapping after former conviction of two or more felonies and his sentence of life imprisonment.

Hinkle v. State


No. F-86-86


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1989 OK CR 4; 771 P.2d 232; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5



March 20, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended April 5, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, The Honorable Don Powers, District Judge. Oren Richard Hinkle, appellant, was convicted of Oral Sodomy and Attempted Rape in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Case No. CRF-85-536, was sentenced to one (1) year and twenty (20) years, respectively, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  The conviction for Oral Sodomy is REVERSED and REMANDED for a new trial. The conviction for Attempted Rape is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) convicting him of oral sodomy and attempted rape.


OVERVIEW: The victim, a 76-year old widow, was walking home when defendant grabbed her from behind and forced her into his truck. He ordered the victim to take off her skirt and forced her to commit oral sodomy and sexual intercourse. When a car approached, the victim screamed for help, opened the car door, and fell to the ground. Defendant drove away. Defendant alleged that the oral sodomy was consensual and that there was no sexual intercourse. The court held that the State was not required to prove force as an element of oral sodomy but that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that consent was not a defense. However, the trial court did not err in instructing the jury on the lesser-included offense of attempted rape based on the victim's testimony regarding defendant's attempts at penetration. The victim's testimony did not require corroboration because it remained unwavering throughout trial. Further, sufficient corroboration existed including evidence of fresh lacerations in the victim's genital area, a hair found on the victim's skirt that was consistent with defendant's hair, and the testimony of the individual who approached defendant's car during the assault.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for oral sodomy and remanded for a new trial. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted rape.

Drew v. State


No. F-87-198


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1989 OK CR 1; 771 P.2d 224; 1989 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2



February 28, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, The Honorable James Gullett, District Judge. Karen June Drew, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the First Degree in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Case No. CRF-85-374. In accordance with the jury's recommendation, she was sentenced to a term of life imprisonment. From said judgment and sentence, appellant appeals to this Court.



DISPOSITION:  Judgment and sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted her of murder in the first degree and sentenced her to a term of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder in connection with the death of her daughter. On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that (1) the State failed to prove that she caused the death of her daughter; (2) Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(C) (Supp. 1982) was unconstitutional; and (3) the trial court erred in admitting evidence of child abuse and in failing to give a limiting instruction concerning the use of such evidence. Upon review, the court found defendant's arguments without merit. Medical testimony revealed that the fatal injury most likely occurred within 12 hours of the child's arrival at the hospital. Based on the evidence, any rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant inflicted the injury which caused the death of her daughter. The instruction given was not coercive. The State's evidence clearly tended to establish that the child's death was not the result of an accident. Therefore, such evidence was admissible.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for first degree murder were affirmed.

State v. Johnson


No. S-87-412


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 273; 765 P.2d 1226; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 288



November 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the Tulsa County District Court, The Honorable Gordon D. McAllister, District Judge. The State appealed on a reserved question of law from the dismissal by the Tulsa County District Court which held 21 O.S.1981, § 863 unconstitutional based on the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Tulsa County District Court (Oklahoma), which dismissed a charge of concealing the stillbirth of a child against defendant finding that the statute violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with concealing the stillbirth of a child that was born to her out of wedlock. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss finding that the statute unconstitutionally discriminated against unwed mothers and illegitimate children. On appeal, the court reversed finding that the mothers and fathers of children born out of wedlock were not similarly situated because the mother would inevitably be present at the birth of the child, and therefore it was logical that she was the person charged with the responsibility for reporting the death. The court found that the mother of an illegitimate child had the sole responsibility of caring for and maintaining the child. The court found that in light of the importance of deaths being reported in order to allow for accurate medical research and statistics, the requirement was not archaic and substantially furthered the objective of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and ordered that the state could not bring further action against defendant in the matter.

 

894 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


A.M.H. v. State


No. J-88-276


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 269; 766 P.2d 351; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 281



November 18, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Delaware County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Martha Sue Thompson, Special District Judge. Appellant, A.M.H., was charged in Delaware County District Court, Case No. CRF-87-187, for the offense of first degree murder. After a preliminary examination including a prosecutive merit hearing in which appellant's motion to certify him to the Juvenile Division of the Court was denied, appellant was bound over to stand trial as an adult.



DISPOSITION:  JUDGMENT OF MAGISTRATE DENYING A MOTION TO CERTIFY appellant as a juvenile is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile was charged with first degree murder under the reverse certification statute. He filed a motion for certification as a juvenile under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2 (1986). The juvenile appealed after a magistrate of the District Court, Delaware County, Oklahoma, denied his motion.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile shot and killed his grandmother while she slept. He was later picked up in another town as a runaway. He was not considered a suspect in the murder but was questioned in his mother's presence as to what he knew about the homicide. An officer testified that he spoke with the juvenile alone for five minutes and that the juvenile decided to confess. His mother returned and was present for the confession. At that time, he was not charged with first degree murder; thus, mandatory adult certification under § 1104.2 did not apply. His motion to suppress the confession was overruled. The juvenile argued that his confession was inadmissible under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1109 (1986) because it resulted from the officer's "secretive questioning." However, he did not address the five-minute period in his brief, and the officer's testimony reflected that he did not question the juvenile. Thus, the court held that the suppression motion was properly overruled. The magistrate's ruling was properly limited to the prospective merit hearing only. Sufficient evidence supported the juvenile's certification for trial as an adult. The adult certification statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision to deny the juvenile's motion for certification as a juvenile was affirmed.

Gilbert v. State


No. 0-87-637


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 268; 765 P.2d 1208; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 295



November 18, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma The Honorable Gordon McAllister, Special Judge. Bobby L. Gilbert, appellant, entered pleas of nolo contendere to four counts of Violation of a Protective Order in the District Court of Tulsa County. He received a six (6) month suspended sentence on each count. The State filed applications to revoke the suspended sentences, alleging further violations of the protective order. This appeal is brought from the order of the District Court revoking the suspended sentences. Finding no basis for reversal, the orders of the District Court of Tulsa County are AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from orders of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which granted the State's applications to revoke suspended sentences imposed on defendant. The sentences had been imposed after defendant pled nolo contendere to four counts of violating a protective order issued pursuant to Oklahoma's Protection from Domestic Violence Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 60 et seq. (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife obtained a protective order pursuant to the Act that ordered defendant not to visit with, assault, molest, or otherwise interfere with her, not to threaten her, and to remain away from her residence. After defendant pled guilty to violating the order, he received suspended sentences. When defendant made threatening phone calls to his former wife in further violation of the protective order, the State sought revocation of the suspended sentences. The trial court revoked the suspended sentences and, on appeal, the court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's argument that the Act was unconstitutionally vague, explaining that the term "visit" in Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 60.4(D)(2) (1987), in its ordinary sense, meant a personal confrontation initiated by the enjoined person and that the phrase "otherwise interfere" clearly meant interference of the same general character, kind, nature, or class as visit, assault, molest, or harass. The court further held that the term "visit" was not unconstitutionally overbroad because it was subject to a narrow construction which did not have a real and substantial effect on any legitimate and constitutionally protected speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

Hale v. State


No. F-87-951


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 263; 764 P.2d 1360; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 270

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, The Honorable James L. Gullett, District Judge. Patricia Ann Hale, appellant, was convicted in the District Court of Oklahoma County of Possession of a Controlled Dangerous Substance, Dihydromorphinone; Possession of a Controlled Dangerous Substance, Oxycodone; Possession of a Controlled Dangerous Substance, Diazepam; Possession of Controlled Dangerous Substance, Phenmetrazine; and two counts of Possession of a Weapon While Committing a Felony. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted her of possession of controlled dangerous substances including oxycodone, diazepam and phenmetrazine, and possession of a weapon while committing a felony.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from her convictions defendant claimed that the statute under which she was convicted of possession of a weapon, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1287 (1987), was unconstitutional because it read, "Use of firearm or other offensive weapon while committing or attempting to commit a felony-Penalties," and the body of the statute punished mere possession, it violated Okla. Const. art. V, § 57. Some of them dated back thirty years and involved forged instruments. None of the arrests resulted in criminal prosecution, much less conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial.

Johnson v. State


No. F-86-917


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 242; 764 P.2d 197; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 241



October 19, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, The Honorable William R. Saied, District Judge.  [***1] Marvin E. Johnson, appellant, was convicted of possession of a controlled dangerous substance after former conviction of two or more felonies, in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Case No. CRF-86-588, sentenced to forty (40) years imprisonment, and appeals. AFFIRMED.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by a jury and sentence in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), for possession of a controlled dangerous substance after former conviction of two or more felonies.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was lawfully arrested for public intoxication. Before placing him in the patrol car, the officers searched him, found a small bottle containing PCP in his right front pocket, and additionally arrested him for possession of PCP. Defendant claimed that the officers found the bottle of PCP on the ground after his arrest, not in his pocket. The trial court denied his motion to suppress the PCP. Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of a controlled dangerous substance after former conviction of two or more felonies. The court held that the trial court did not err by permitting the prosecutor to elicit details of defendant's former convictions on cross-examination because defendant had opened the door to inquiry on the issue in his direct examination. The trial court did not err in enhancing defendant's sentence because defendant did not meet his burden of proving that his prior convictions arose from the same transaction or occurrence. The trial court did not err in refusing to suppress the PCP. The PCP was discovered during a warrantless search that was reasonable because it was incident to the lawful arrest of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Nguyen v. State


No. F-86-786


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 240; 769 P.2d 167; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 238



October 14, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended November 12, 1988; Rehearing Denied February 9, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma The Honorable Jay D. Dalton, District Judge. Tuan Anh Nguyen, appellant, was convicted in Tulsa County District Court, Case No. CRF-82-1986, of three counts of Murder in the First Degree. He was sentenced to life imprisonment for Count I, and death for Counts II and III, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of three counts of Murder in the First Degree. He was sentenced to life imprisonment for Count I and death for Counts II and III.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed to death his three victims. One of the victims was his wife and the other two victims were minors who were related to her. He was subsequently, apprehended and convicted. He sought review. On appeal, the court upheld the convictions and sentences. The court rejected defendant's argument that his right to equal protection was violated by the prosecutor's exclusion of three blacks from the jury panel by the use of peremptory challenges. The court ruled that because defendant was Vietnamese, not Black, Batson was inapplicable. The court further found that the prosecutor provided an explanation for challenging each of the black veniremen. The court held that the purpose of the State's duty to give notice of its intention to introduce evidence of other crimes at trial was to insure against surprise on part of the defense, and to allow time for the defense to be heard prior to the information being placed before the jury. The court concluded that the fact that the pictures of the murder victims were gruesome had not, of itself, caused the photographs to be inadmissible. The court found that the probative value of the photographs were manifested in numerous ways.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

899 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Newsom v. State


No. F-86-53


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 229; 763 P.2d 135; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 249



October 12, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Comanche County, The Honorable William M. Roberts, District Judge.  [***1] Michael Edward Newsom, appellant, was convicted of First Degree Rape, First Degree Burglary and Crime Against Nature, Sodomy, all After Former Conviction of Two Felonies, in the District Court of Comanche County, Case No. CRF-85-41, was sentenced to twenty-five (25) years, twenty (20) years, and twenty-five (25) years, respectively, the terms to run consecutively, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first degree rape, first degree burglary, and crime against nature, sodomy, and sentenced him to consecutive terms.


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into the prosecutrix' home, forced her to commit oral sodomy on him, raped her, and stole items from her home. She was able to see what he was wearing and described it to a neighbor. At trial, the neighbor identified defendant as the man he had seen outside the prosecutrix' home. On appeal, defendant argued the neighbor's identification testimony should not have been admitted. The court held that the pre-trial photographic line-ups did not taint the neighbor's in-court identification and any prior misidentification went to the weight, not admissibility of his testimony. Defendant argued that use of force was an element of the crime of sodomy and the state had not been required to prove it. The court found that use of force was only needed where the sex was consensual and there was no allegation by defendant that the prosecutrix had consented. The information which charged defendant with burglary was sufficient because defendant was not misled by it and the jury instruction accurately defined the elements. Finally, the owner of the trailer where the owner and defendant lived had authority to consent to a search of the trailer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence.

McBrain v. State


No. F-86-690


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 218; 763 P.2d 121; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 229



September 27, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Kay County, Oklahoma The Honorable Kenneth Reed, District Judge.  [***1] Kirk Warren McBrain, appellant, was convicted in the District Court of Noble County, Case No. CRF-85-06 of the crimes of Kidnapping, First Degree Rape (two counts) and Sodomy. Appellant was sentenced to eight (8) years imprisonment on the Kidnapping charge, ten (10) years imprisonment on each of the Rape counts (each count to run concurrently) and ten (10) years imprisonment on the Sodomy charge. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the District Court of Kay County (Oklahoma), defendant was convicted of sodomy, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981), kidnapping, and two counts of first degree rape. For his crimes, defendant was sentenced to concurrent sentences of 10 years' imprisonment on the sodomy charge, 8 years' imprisonment on the kidnapping charge, and 10 years' imprisonment on each of the rape charges. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his two companions abducted a 14-year-old girl. Defendant watched while his companions raped the girl and, thereafter, defendant forced the girl to orally sodomize him. Subsequently, defendant was convicted of sodomy, kidnapping, and two counts of first degree rape and sentenced accordingly. In affirming, the court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981), the statute criminalizing sodomy, was constitutional. Furthermore, the court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's denial of defendant's second motion for change of venue. The court noted that the trial court granted defendant's first request for a change of venue. The court found that there was nothing in the record to show that defendant did not receive a fair and impartial trial, despite the trial court's unwillingness to grant a second motion for change of venue. The court rejected defendant's contention that there was insufficient evidence to conclude that defendant aided and abetted in his companions' commission of the rapes. Lastly, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions and that no modification of the sentence was warranted based on the facts of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction and sentence.

Roth v. State

Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 200; 762 P.2d 279; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 198

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Comanche County. CRM-85-372 and CRM-85-372, was sentenced to six (6) months on each count, to run consecutively, and appeals. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma), which convicted her of two counts of solicitation for prostitution in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1029 (1981) and Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1030 (1981), and sentenced her to six months on each count, to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried by jury and convicted of two counts of solicitation for prostitution in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1029 (1981) and Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1030 (1981). The jury set punishment at six months for each count, to run consecutively. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed because defendant did not have standing to challenge the language of the statute as overbroad because she was not charged with soliciting indiscriminate sexual intercourse without hire. Rather, she was charged and convicted of soliciting by offering sexual intercourse for hire. In addition, the evidence was sufficient to support the finding of guilt because the State presented the testimony of two police officers, who stated that defendant offered sex for money. They also testified that the house and location of the offense was known to rent rooms to prostitutes for 30-minute intervals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence of the trial court.

H.W. v. State


No. J-88-79


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 138; 759 P.2d 214; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 139



July 15, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Craig County, The Honorable Jess B. Clanton, Associate District Judge. H.W., a juvenile appellant, was charged as an adult with three (3) counts of first degree murder pursuant to the reverse certification statute, in the District Court of Craig County, Case No. CRF-87-81. Appellant's motion to be certified as a child was denied, and she appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile was charged in the District Court of Craig County (Oklahoma) with three counts of First Degree Malice Aforethought Murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1981) pursuant to the Reverse Certification Statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2 (1986). The trial court denied defendant's motion to be certified as a child under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104(C) (1986) and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 16-years-old, asserted that her statements made to Texas authorities were inadmissible because they were made outside the presence of her parents, guardian, attorney, or legal custodian as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1109(A) (1986). The court affirmed and found that under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2(A), any person aged 16 or 17 and charged with murder was considered an adult. The court held that the legislature did not intend to afford protections of the juvenile statutes to those who fell under the Reverse Certification Statute. The court rejected defendant's assertion that the serving of her uncle was not service of her "next friend" as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1004.2 (1986). The court found that defendant was accused of the murder of her father, her stepmother, and her half-sister. The court found no evidence that the guardian appointed after the death of defendant's mother was the guardian of defendant's person. The court held the trial court properly found that based on defendant's history of drug and alcohol abuse, along with her psychological problems, the public would not be protected if defendant were processed by the juvenile system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

903 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Plotner v. State


No. F-84-772


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 139; 762 P.2d 936; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 140



July 15, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Rehear Denied August 30, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, the Honorable Karl R. Gray, District Judge. Ralph Edward Plotner, Jr., appellant, was convicted of Attempted First Degree Rape and Forcible Sodomy, in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Case No. CRF-83-6297, sentenced respectively to fifteen (15) and five (5) years imprisonment, and appeals. AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for attempted first-degree rape and forcible sodomy from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), arguing that the information was fatally defective because it omitted and inadequately described essential elements of attempted rape and did not properly plead the offense of forcible sodomy.


OVERVIEW: Upon the prosecutrix' and other's testimony, defendant was convicted of forcible sodomy and attempted first-degree rape. Defendant challenged his conviction. As to the latter charge, the prosecution contended that the overt act required to be stated in the information was sufficiently described by the words, "attempted to have sexual intercourse with (the prosecutrix) by means of force." The court disagreed and reversed defendant's conviction. The words merely repeated the legal definition of rape, in essence stating that defendant committed attempted rape by attempting to commit rape. The information described no overt physical act or actual personal threat towards the commission of the crime. Therefore, the information was fatally defective in failing to describe the overt act with sufficient specificity. Even assuming that a liberal construction might have saved the "overt act" deficiency, there was no mention of the requisite "intent" to commit rape. As for defendant's challenge to the forcible sodomy count, the court found that although the language and syntax were clumsy, the meaning was sufficiently clear to appraise defendant of what he was to defend against at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for forcible sodomy, but reversed his conviction for attempted first degree rape and remanded on that basis with instructions to sustain the demurrer to the information.

Munson v. State


No. F-85-479


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 124; 758 P.2d 324; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 135



June 24, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended June 29, 1988; Petition for Rehearing Denied July 20, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Custer County The Honorable Gary McGinn, District Judge. Adolph Honel Munson, appellant, was convicted of First Degree Murder (Count I), Kidnapping (Count II), and Robbery With Firearms (Count III), in the District Court of Custer County, Case No. CRF-84-129, sentenced respectively to death, ten (10) years, and forty (40) years imprisonment, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Counts I and II AFFIRMED. Count III REVERSED and REMANDED with instructions to DISMISS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court of Custer County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first degree murder, kidnapping, and robbery with firearms. Defendant was sentenced respectively to death, 10 years, and 40 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of pre-trial issues, defendant contended that the trial court erred in failing to provide funds for the services of an expert serologist, an expert in hair analysis, and an investigator. The trial court denied the funds and advised defendant's counsel that he would have to pay for such services and then seek reimbursement for the expenses incurred in the representation of his indigent client from the Oklahoma Supreme Court. The court held that defendant's argument was without merit because the effective assistance guarantee of the due process clause required a reversal from a denial of such assistance only if defendant established prejudice by clear and convincing evidence. The court held that defendant failed to demonstrate substantial prejudice from the lack of the expert and investigative assistance. Regarding his trial, defendant argued that the trial court was without jurisdiction to instruct the jury on first degree felony-murder where the information charged first degree malice aforethought murder. The court held that where an information charged first degree malice aforethought murder, a conviction was proper for felony-murder if supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted and sentenced defendant.

Bromley v. State


No. C-85-735


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 120; 757 P.2d 382; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 144



June 15, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Grady County The Honorable James R. Winchester, District Judge LOUIS J. BROMLEY, appellant, pled guilty to First Degree Robbery-Murder in the District Court of Grady County, before the Honorable James R. Winchester, in Case No. CRF-85-10. After a sentencing hearing, appellant was sentenced to death. The petition for writ of certiorari is DENIED. The death sentence is MODIFIED to life imprisonment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a writ of certiorari regarding his guilty plea to first degree robbery murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(b) (1981) and his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed a pharmacist during a drug store robbery, and he pled guilty to first-degree robbery murder. After a hearing, defendant was sentenced to death. The court denied defendant's petition for a writ of certiorari, holding that the trial court made a sufficient determination of defendant's competency. After a review of the entire record, the court concluded that defendant knowingly waived his right against self-incrimination. The transcript failed to disclose any support for defendant's claimed misunderstanding of the discretionary aspect of withdrawing a guilty plea. However, defendant was denied due process by the imposition of the death sentence because that sentence was based in part on evidence of a prior murder charge that had been dismissed after defendant's right to a speedy trial had been violated. The trial court correctly refused to introduce a mitigating letter when that letter had no indicia of reliability. However, the trial court erred in refusing to consider mitigating evidence contained in the preliminary hearing transcript.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's petition for a writ of certiorari but modified his sentence to life imprisonment.

Brennan v. State

Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 119

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA THE HONORABLE WILLIAM S. MYERS, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE MARK EDWARD BRENNAN, appellant, pled guilty to Burglary in the First Degree and Murder in the First Degree in Oklahoma County District Court, Case No. CRF-84-5330. He received sentences of ten years' imprisonment and the death penalty, respectively. Judgments and sentences are AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a sentence of ten years' imprisonment and a death penalty imposed by the Oklahoma County District Court (Oklahoma) following defendant's guilty plea to the crimes of first-degree burglary and first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to the crime of first-degree murder and first-degree burglary. The trial judgment conducted a hearing to receive evidence of aggravating and mitigating factors, at the end of which he imposed ten years' imprisonment for the burglary, and the death penalty on the murder conviction. The court found no indication in the record that the presence of television cameras in the courtroom disrupted the proceedings or adversely impacted the trial participants, or that the trial judge was pressured into giving the death penalty because of the media presence. There was a sufficient factual basis for accepting defendant's pleas of guilty. Defendant failed to overcome the presumption that the trial judge considered incompetent or irrelevant evidence. The sentence of death was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or other arbitrary factors. Both aggravating circumstances and the existence of future dangerousness to society were sufficiently supported by the evidence. The evidence supported a finding that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel in that it was preceded by torture or serious physical abuse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's judgment of conviction and sentences imposed by the trial court.

DUTTON v. DIXON


No. P-88-56


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 107; 757 P.2d 376; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 120



May 25, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding from the District Court of Oklahoma County, The Honorable Bryan Dixon, District Judge. Lonnie Joe Dutton, petitioner, was convicted of First Degree Murder, in Oklahoma County District Court, Case No. CRF-79-105, sentenced to death and, following vacation of death sentence by Tenth Circuit Court of Appeals, files an application for a writ of prohibition to prohibit resentencing. WRIT GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an application for writs of prohibition and mandamus to prohibit resentencing under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, §701.13(E)(2) (1985) after the vacation of his death sentence by the Tenth Circuit Court of Appeals (Oklahoma). Defendant had been convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentence to death. The Tenth Circuit Court of Appeals affirmed the U.S. District Court's denial of habeas corpus relief but vacated defendant's death sentence after holding that the trial court erred in refusing to allow defendant's mother to testify. It directed the district court to issue a writ of habeas corpus, modifying defendant's sentence to life imprisonment unless the State commenced new sentencing proceedings. Defendant then filed an application for a writ of prohibition to prevent the district court judge from conducting a capital resentencing trial under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13(E)(2) (1985). The court granted the writ, finding that under the previous version of the death sentence review statute, § 701.13(E)(2) (1981), where errors occurred during the sentencing stage of a capital trial, the court had modified the death sentence to life imprisonment. The court held that the 1985 version of the statute could not be applied retroactively without violating the ex post facto clause of U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10 because it would deprive defendant of the right to have his death sentence modified to life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writs of prohibition and mandamus sought by defendant to prohibit the district court from conducting a resentencing trial after his death sentence had been vacated.

Phillips v. State


No. F-86-514


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 103; 756 P.2d 604; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 104



May 18, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied June 24, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, The Honorable Jay D. Dalton, District Judge.  [***1] Reginald L. Phillips, appellant, was convicted of First Degree Rape, First Degree Burglary, two counts of Forcible Sodomy, Assault and Battery with a Dangerous Weapon, and Feloniously Pointing a Weapon, in the District Court of Tulsa County, Case No. CRF-85-3055, sentenced respectively to imprisonment for twenty-five (25) years, ten (10) years, thirteen (13) years, thirteen (13) years, ten (10) years, and ten (10) years, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED in part and AFFIRMED in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first degree rape, first degree burglary, two counts of forcible sodomy, assault and battery with a dangerous weapon, and feloniously pointing a weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the victim's home through a window, surprised the victim in bed, threatened her with a knife and later with her own gun, and raped her. He was convicted of rape, burglary, and forcible sodomy for fellatio and cunnilingus, assault and battery, and feloniously pointing a weapon. Defendant was sentenced to serve consecutive terms of imprisonment for each offense. Defendant appealed. The court reverse his sodomy conviction for cunnilingus and otherwise affirmed. A self-serving out-of-court statement made by defendant to an arresting officer was properly excluded from trial because it constituted hearsay. Although admissible after defendant opened the issue, character evidence was excluded from trial, and the state's attempt to introduce evidence of mendacity was proper. The victim's in-court identification was inherently reliable. Because the State failed to prove the essential element of penetration, the court held that it had no alternative but to reverse the conviction for oral sodomy or cunnilingus and to remand with instructions to dismiss. The evidence otherwise supported the jury's verdict, and the punishment was within the statutory range.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for forcible sodomy (cunnilingus) and remanded the charge with instructions to dismiss. The court affirmed the remaining convictions and sentences.

S.A.H. v. State


No. J-88-58


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 71; 753 P.2d 381; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 79



April 6, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied April 18, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Creek County, The Honorable BILL WILSON, Special District Judge. S.A.H., appellant, was charged and bound over on two counts of First Degree Murder, two counts of Kidnapping, two counts of Robbery With Firearms, two counts of Larceny of an Automobile, and one count of Third Degree Arson, in the District Court of Creek County, Case No. CRF-87-240, and appeals from an order denying his motion to be certified as a juvenile. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a 17-year-old juvenile, challenged an order of the Creek County District Court (Oklahoma), which denied his motion to be certified as a juvenile and bound him over for trial. The state charged defendant as an adult under the Reverse Certification Statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2 (Supp. 1986) with, inter alia, two counts of first-degree murder and two counts of kidnapping. The court had stayed the trial pending the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 1104.2 violated the Cruel and Unusual Punishment Clause of the Eighth Amendment because of the potential for execution of a person less than 18 years of age. The court noted that it had reaffirmed its prior holding that imposition of the death penalty on a juvenile who was 15 years old at the time of the offense constituted neither cruel nor unusual punishment where the minor had been certified as an adult. However, the court declined to address whether the same result would obtain under the reverse certification statute because this issue had been prematurely raised. Eighth Amendment scrutiny was appropriate only after the state had secured a formal adjudication of guilt, so as to acquire the power to punish; defendant had not been tried, convicted, or sentenced. The court rejected defendant's argument that § 1104.2 violated both substantive due process and equal protection standards of review. Statutes were presumptively constitutional, and the challenging party had the burden of proving otherwise. The court affirmed and concluded that the district court did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court vacated its prior stay of the proceedings and affirmed the order of the district court.

Harris v. Okla. County Dist. Court


No. P-88-50


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 26; 750 P.2d 1129; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 48



February 12, 1988, Decided  
February 12, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Directing Publication February 18, 1988.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an individual, who was found not guilty of first degree murder by reason of insanity, but was ordered to be placed under state psychiatric care, filed an application for a writ of prohibition to prohibit respondents, the Oklahoma County District Court and the State of Oklahoma, from retaining jurisdiction in the criminal proceedings against him.


OVERVIEW: After petitioner was found not guilty by reason of insanity, the district court ordered his release from incarceration, but thereafter, issued an order directing that petitioner be placed under state psychiatric care. Petitioner filed an application for a writ prohibiting the district court from retaining jurisdiction in his criminal case. The court stayed the proceedings until the hearing on the application. Petitioner argued that the district court lacked jurisdiction over him because jurisdiction was relinquished by the order of his release from incarceration. The court denied the writ, holding that the district court erred by releasing petitioner without a determination that he was not presently mentally ill and dangerous to the public as required by Okla. The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1161 (1981) was not unconstitutional and did not deprive him of due process as the statute required an examination for 30 days and a hearing within 45 days.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for a writ to prohibit the State and the district court from retaining jurisdiction over his criminal proceedings.

Douma v. State


No. F-85-382


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 19; 749 P.2d 1163; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 21



January 29, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by Douma v. Workman, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 59487 (N.D. Okla., Aug. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Joe Jennings, District Judge. Davin Jake Douma, the appellant, was convicted in the District Court of Tulsa County, Case No. CRF-84-1661, of First Degree Murder for which he received a sentence of life imprisonment, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma that convicted defendant of first-degree murder for which he received a sentence of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. The court affirmed. The court found that the Reverse Certification Statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2 (1981), was not unconstitutional because the implementation of § 1104.2 acted as a deterrent to those who believed 16 and 17 year olds could violate the law with impunity. There was no error in the admission of witnesses' testimony regarding events that took place one week after the murder, as the statements about defendant's intentions to "waste a queer" constituted subsequent inculpatory statements and the admission was not an abuse of discretion. The trial court did not err when it refused to allow individual voir dire. Because defendant did not exhaust his peremptory challenges, he could not allege the bias of a juror on appeal. There was no abuse of discretion in admitting photographic evidence. Even if it was error to admit evidence of defendant's prior crimes, the admission was harmless, as the State's case against defendant was overwhelming. Defendant's allegations that he was denied the right of confrontation, that the jury instructions were inadequate, and that his trial counsel was ineffective were meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Hale v. State


No. F-84-208


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 24; 750 P.2d 130; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 20



January 29, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 2, 1988; As Amended March 17, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Pottawatomie County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Gary R. Brown, District Judge. Alvie James Hale, Jr., appellant, was convicted in the District Court of Pottawatomie County, Case No. CRF-83-348, of Murder in the First Degree and Kidnapping for Extortion. He received the death penalty and life imprisonment, respectively.



DISPOSITION:  Judgments and sentences are AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment in the District Court of Pottawatomie County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of murder in the first degree and kidnapping for extortion, then sentenced him to the death penalty and life imprisonment, respectively. The victim's body was found on defendant's father's property, with a great deal of physical evidence implicating defendant. Defendant was convicted of a federal extortion crime on the same facts.


OVERVIEW: The victim's family received a series of ransom calls from an unidentified man that were linked to defendant, and federal agents caught him with the money after pursuing him from the ransom site. The trial court refused to change venue in the case, but it removed all jurors challenged for cause. Although all jurors knew something about the case or someone connected to it, each juror said they could render an impartial decision. On review, the court found no reversible error in the jury selection process, found that extortion was not a lesser included offense of kidnapping for extortion, and that the evidence did not support manslaughter or second degree murder instructions. The court rejected double jeopardy arguments and found several errors to be harmless, not properly preserved for review, or lacking prejudicial effect. The court found that the probative value of pictures of the body outweighed their prejudicial effect, and that it was not ineffective for defense counsel not to object to admissible evidence or acceptable prosecution remarks. The court rejected challenges to the constitutional sufficiency of Oklahoma's death penalty statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and sentences.

 

914 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Glenn v. State


No. F-85-750


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1988 OK CR 16; 749 P.2d 121; 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13



January 13, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Alan J. Couch, Associate District Judge. JERRY WAYNE GLENN, ALFRED EUGENE PERRY and JOHN LEE PHELPS, the appellants, were each convicted in the District Court of Cleveland County of Exhibiting Obscene Motion Pictures. Glenn, Case No. CRF-84-1368, was convicted of five counts and sentenced to one year of imprisonment on each count. Perry, Case No. CRF-84-1366, was convicted of two counts and fined $ 100.00 on each count. Phelps, Case No. CRF-84-1367 was also convicted of two counts and fined $ 100.00 on each count, and they appeal.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the owner and two employees of an adult bookstore, challenged an order of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which convicted the owner of five counts of exhibiting obscene motion pictures and sentenced him to one year in prison on each count. The employees were convicted of two counts of exhibiting obscene motion pictures and were fined $ 100 on each count.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that the obscenity statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1024.1 (Supp. 1986) was unconstitutional because it contained so many value judgments that a person could not know with reasonable certainty whether he was committing a crime. The court held that § 1024.1 provided a fair notice to defendants that they were subject to prosecution. Further, § 1024.1 was constitutionally applied. The employees claimed that they were exempt from liability under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1040.53 (1981). The court concluded that the employees were not exempted by § 1040.53 because an adult bookstore that provided individual booths for viewing token-operated videotapes did not fit within the definition of a commercial motion picture theater set out in § 1040.53. The employees also claimed that their actions did not amount to an "exhibition within the meaning of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1021 (Supp. 1986). The court held that because the employees were responsible for keeping the store open for business, and because obscene videotape jackets were openly on display, there was sufficient evidence for the jury to determine that they were principals in the exhibition of the videotapes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and sentences of the trial court.

Lambert v. State


No. M-87-78


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 246; 745 P.2d 1185; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 519



November 13, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended December 22, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Kay County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Neal Beekman, District Judge. John Edward Lambert, Jr., appellant, was convicted in the District Court of Kay County Case No. CRF-86-50 of the crimes of Driving Under the Influence of Alcohol, [Text Deleted by Court Emendation] (Count I), and Driving While License is Revoked (Count II). He was fined $ 1,000.00 and sentenced to twelve (12) months in jail on Count I; fined $ 250.00 and sentenced to three (3) months in jail on (Count II), and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED IN PART, AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Kay County (Oklahoma) convicted defendant of driving under the influence of alcohol and driving on a revoked license. The district court imposed consecutive sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a single car accident and walked from the vehicle to a nearby house. The occupant knew defendant and gave him a ride home. On the way home, the occupant stopped at the accident site and told the patrolman that he had taken defendant home, that defendant seemed to have been drinking, and that defendant had been injured. The occupant then took the patrolman to defendant's house. The occupant knocked on the door, called out to defendant, asking him if he was still there and if he was okay. Defendant responded by saying "yes," at which point the occupant and the patrolman entered the house. After talking with defendant, the patrolman arrested defendant for driving under the influence. Defendant argued that his warrantless arrest was unconstitutional. The court held that the warrantless intrusion into defendant's home was per se unreasonable and that no exigent circumstances justified the entrance and subsequent arrest. Therefore, the court reversed defendant's conviction for driving under the influence. The court affirmed defendant's other conviction, however, because defendant failed to cite relevant authority to support his proposition of error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for driving under the influence and affirmed defendant's conviction for driving on a revoked license.

Morgan v. State


No. C-86-169


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 234; 744 P.2d 1280; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 506



October 27, 1987, Filed

Dalton, District Judge James Calvin Morgan, petitioner, pled nolo contendere and was convicted of Forcible Sodomy in the District Court of Tulsa County, Case No. CRF-85-2319, sentenced to four (4) years imprisonment, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of his sodomy conviction and four-year sentence imposed by the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), asserting the improper denial of his request to withdraw his plea.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner entered a plea of nolo contendere to the charge of forcible sodomy in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21 § 888 (1981). The trial court accepted the plea and imposed a four-year sentence. Petitioner sought to withdraw his plea and the trial court denied the request. Thereafter, petitioner filed a petition for writ of certiorari. The court assumed jurisdiction and noted that petitioner's desire to withdraw the plea was based upon his misunderstanding that his plea would result in a suspended sentence. This conclusion was based upon the erroneous assumption regarding petitioner's prior record. However, the court noted that the trial court had determined that the sentence was proper in light of the seriousness of the crime, regardless of the prior conviction. Because petitioner entered his plea without the promise of leniency and with its attendant risks, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the request to withdraw the plea.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's judgment and sentence were affirmed and the petition for certiorari was denied.

Crouch v. State


No. F-85-684


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 222; 744 P.2d 971; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 501



October 15, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 18, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Latimer County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Robert W. Moore, Associate District Judge. Cynthia Lea Crouch, appellant, was convicted in the District Court of Latimer County, Case No. CRF-84-33, of Embezzlement and False Accounts by Officers for which she received a sentence of two and one-half years' imprisonment, a fine of five hundred dollars ($ 500.00), and was required to pay restitution in the amount of forty-five thousand dollars ($ 45,000.00) within four years, and she appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Latimer County (Oklahoma), which convicted her of embezzlement and false accounts by officers, and sentenced her to two and one-half years, and a fine of $ 500, and additionally required restitution of $ 45,000. Defendant claimed that the trial judge displayed bias against her and the restitution order was not supported by sufficient proof and was arbitrary and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was the secretary/treasurer of the water department, deposited cash received by the water department to bank accounts that she and her husband maintained. On appeal from a conviction for embezzlement, defendant claimed that the trial court failed to hold an adequate hearing to determine the impact of threatening telephone calls that were made to at least two jurors during the trial. The court held that this assignment of error had no merit because defendant's counsel did not ask for a hearing or object to the instruction the trial court gave on the subject. Defendant also failed to properly preserve an assignment of error based on the trial judge's alleged display of prejudice toward defendant. Finally, the court rejected defendant's claim that the sentence and restitution she was ordered to pay was excessive and irrational. The sentence was within the range provided by the applicable statute and did not shock the court's conscience. The restitution order was not an abuse of discretion because it was related to the amount that defendant embezzled and there was no evidence that the restitution would impose manifest hardship on defendant or her family.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence was affirmed.
