Castro v. State


No. F-84-378


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 182; 745 P.2d 394; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 461



August 28, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Filed September 17, 1987; Opinion on Rehearing Denied November 24, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Kay County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Roger Mullins, Associate District Judge. John W. Castro, Sr., appellant, was convicted of First Degree Murder under the felony-murder doctrine, and Robbery With Firearms in the District Court of Kay County, Oklahoma, Case No. CRF-83-130, sentenced to death, and life imprisonment respectively, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Judgment and sentence of death for first degree felony-murder is AFFIRMED, and judgment and sentence of life imprisonment for robbery with firearms is VACATED and remanded with instructions to DISMISS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Kay County (Oklahoma), which had convicted him of first degree murder under the felony murder doctrine, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(B) (1981), and robbery with firearms, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 801 (Supp. 1982), and imposed sentences of death and life imprisonment on the convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted based on a slaying of an employee at a fast-food restaurant. The death sentence was based on the aggravating circumstances of especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel and continuing threat to society. The court found that: (1) there had been no error in refusing funds for a psychiatrist or for obtaining certain witness testimony; (2) challenges to the jury selection were meritless where the exclusion of a juror for opposition to the death penalty was proper and the jury did constitute a cross-section of the community despite the exclusion of jurors opposed to capital punishment; (3) any errors in the admission of evidence were harmless, there had been no error in the jury instructions, and the confession of defendant had been knowing and voluntary; (4) the convictions for both murder in the commission of the robbery and the robbery with firearms violated double jeopardy and required vacation of the robbery conviction; and (5) there had been no prosecutorial misconduct or other error in the penalty phase and the state death penalty statute and aggravating circumstances were not unconstitutionally overbroad as applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence of death for first degree felony murder, while vacating the robbery conviction and remanding with instructions to dismiss that conviction.

 

919 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Stouffer v. State


No. F-85-443


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 166; 742 P.2d 562; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 565



 July 31, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Opinion of May 18, 1987, Reported at 738 P.2d 1349.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a rehearing by the court after he was convicted of murder and shooting with intent to kill and received sentences of death and life imprisonment, respectively, and after his conviction and sentences had been affirmed on direct appeal. The court noted that the Tenth Circuit had recently held that the court's construction of the aggravating circumstance of a murder being heinous, atrocious, or cruel was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the aggravating circumstance relating to murder which was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel was applied to him in an overbroad and unconstitutional way, violating the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments. Though the jury was instructed that the aggravating circumstance was limited to deaths preceded by torture or serious physical abuse, the aggravating circumstance had been applied in other cases without requiring such factors; the court thus held that those factors had to be present to apply the aggravating circumstance. The court observed that the evidence against defendant did not support such a finding: the victim was asleep when defendant shot her twice in the head, and there was no reason to believe that she was conscious after the first shot, having expired within minutes. The court concluded that overwhelming evidence of guilt, including two other aggravating circumstances, and rejection of self-defense or accident, made the finding that the murder was heinous, atrocious, or cruel harmless error. When the court reweighed the circumstances, the court found that the death sentence was appropriate. Statutes dealing with competency did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's petition for rehearing except to modify its main opinion by finding that the aggravating circumstance that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel did not apply.

Wood v. Benson


No. H-87-300


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 161; 740 P.2d 1196; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 442



July 28, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An original proceeding in mandamus The Honorable John A. Benson, Associate District Judge. Petitioner, Shayne Wood, a juvenile, seeks issuance of the Writ of Mandamus to require an opportunity to show that he is not an absconder in McCurtain County Juvenile Court, Case No. J-87-14. WRIT GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a juvenile, brought an original proceeding before the court to seek a writ of mandamus. The juvenile sought an opportunity to show that he was not an absconder in Texas. The Texas court based its procedures on the Interstate Compact on Juveniles, Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 532 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile court judge in Texas sent a requisition to the juvenile court judge in Oklahoma, seeking the 17-year-old juvenile's return to face delinquency charges. The Texas authorities asserted that the juvenile intentionally and without the owner's consent entered a building to commit theft. The juvenile contended that he was entitled to an evidentiary hearing to contest the requisition. Without such a hearing, the juvenile claimed that the Compact violated Okla. Const. art. II, §§ 2, 7, 29 and U.S. Const. amend. V, VI, XIV. The court found that the Oklahoma court was ordering the juvenile to be returned to Texas without providing a sufficient hearing. The court noted that whatever the Compact was called, it was in the nature of an extradition proceeding, but no hearing had been held to raise the proper issues. The court agreed that a juvenile was not entitled to all the ramifications and procedures provided in an ordinary criminal trial, but he was entitled to receive sufficient due process to assure fair treatment. The court concluded that the juvenile was to be provided with a sufficient hearing to test the regularity of the requisition, including whether or not he absconded.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the juvenile's case to the juvenile court for further proceedings consistent with the court's decision and granted the juvenile a writ of mandamus.

Staten v. State


No. F-85-385


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 130; 738 P.2d 565; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 413

DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of Kay County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of the crime of driving under the influence of alcohol, second offense. He was sentenced to three years in prison, with two years suspended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the crime of driving under the influence of alcohol, second offense. He was sentenced to three years in prison, with two years suspended. On appeal, the court held that the statute under which defendant was convicted, Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 11-902(A)(1) (1983), was neither vague nor unconstitutional. The court further found that the record clearly showed that defendant was represented by counsel at the time that he entered his guilty pleas to prior crimes of driving under the influence of alcohol. Moreover, defendant did not file an appeal on any of the three prior convictions used for enhancement. Hence, the trial court did not err in denying his motion to suppress his prior convictions. Finally, the court found that defendant had already waived his constitutional right against self-incrimination when he pled guilty in the prior cases. Thus, the trial court did not err in allowing the State to call defendant to testify at the hearing on the motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

AFFIRMED..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his indecent exposure conviction and sentence imposed by the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), urging several grounds of error.


OVERVIEW: While working outside, a store clerk observed defendant four feet away from her masturbating. Thereafter, defendant was convicted of indecent exposure as a prior offender and was sentenced to 10 years' imprisonment, with 6 years suspended. On appeal, he claimed that he was deprived of effective assistance of counsel for counsel's failure to cross-examine the state's witness. The court noted that this decision was a valid trial strategy in light of defendant's alibi defense. Second, defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict. The court noted that the eyewitness clearly viewed defendant in a well-lit area and made positive in-court identification. Because the jury's role was to weigh credibility and to resolve conflicts in testimony, the court deferred to its findings. Next, defendant claimed that the indecent exposure statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1021(1) (1981), was unconstitutional because it placed too much emphasis on the sensitivity of the victim. The court noted that a person of common intelligence would have been offended by defendant's actions and ruled that the statute was constitutional. As such, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal.

Trolinger v. State


No. J-86-876


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 71; 736 P.2d 168; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 350



April 20, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Rogers County, Oklahoma, The Honorable David Allen Box, Special Judge. Appellant, Michael Scott Trolinger, is charged with the offense of First Degree Manslaughter, being a juvenile sixteen years of age he was charged under the reverse certification statute to stand trial as an adult and moved the court to certify him to the Juvenile Court to be treated under the provisions of the juvenile statutes. Appellant's motion to certify him to the juvenile division of the court was denied.



DISPOSITION:  Judgment of the Rogers County District Court declining to certify is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile sought review of the order of the District Court of Rogers County, Oklahoma, which, in defendant's prosecution as an adult for first degree manslaughter pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2 (1981), denied his motion under § 1104.2 for certification as a juvenile.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the denial of his motion, defendant argued that the crime of manslaughter was not proven, that refusal to certify as a juvenile was an abuse of discretion, and that § 1104.2 was unconstitutional. In affirming, the court ruled that, at the preliminary hearing, it was only necessary for the State to show probable cause that a crime had been committed and that defendant committed it. The court found that the evidence showed that a homicide was clearly proven and that defendant admitted he was holding the weapon when it fired. The court ruled that defendant had the burden to sustain his motion to remand to the juvenile division, that the trial court properly considered the factors set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2(C) (1981), and that the determination was not shown to be an abuse of discretion. The court held that the classification created by Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2 bore a rational relationship to the important legislative objective to protect the public and, therefore, was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

925 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State v. Neasbitt


No. S-85-566


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 55; 735 P.2d 337; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 337



March 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Marshall County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Stanley L. Anderson, Associate District Judge. The State of Oklahoma, appellant, appeals a reserved question of law ruled upon by the District Court of Marshall County, in Case No. CRF-84-37. Trial Court's order on reserved question of law is REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order of the District Court of Marshall County (Oklahoma), sustaining defendant's motion in limine to prevent the state from presenting evidence at her trial that she refused to submit to a Breathalyzer test.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, as a prior offender. Her counsel filed a motion in limine to prevent the State from presenting evidence of her refusal to submit to a Breathalyzer test at the time of her arrest. The trial judge held that Okla. Stat. tit. 47 § 756 (1984), which allowed admission of such evidence, was unconstitutional under Okla. Const. art. II, § 21. On appeal, the court noted that where a blood test was physical evidence rather than testimonial, defendant's consent or lack thereof was not within the purview of Okla. Const. art. II, § 21. The court also noted that the U.S. Supreme Court had held that the right to refuse such a test was a matter of legislative grace and that the test was inoffensive to the U.S. Const. amends. IV and V. As such, the court held that the state constitution was not offended by the use of evidence that a driver refused a sobriety test since the test did not implicate the constitutional protection against self-incrimination. As such, the court reversed the trial court's order sustaining the motion in limine.


OUTCOME: The order sustaining the motion in limine was reversed on appeal.

Brecheen v. State


No. F-83-710


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 17; 732 P.2d 889; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 291



January 27, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 3, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Carter County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Woodrow George, District Judge. Robert Allen Brecheen, appellant, was convicted in Carter County District Court, Case No. CRF-83-127, of Burglary in the First Degree and Murder in the First Degree. He received sentences of twenty years' imprisonment and the death penalty, respectively. On his appeal, this Court AFFIRMS all judgments and sentences.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Carter County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first degree murder and first degree burglary and sentenced him to death for the homicide and twenty years' imprisonment for the burglary.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant presented numerous errors, including refusal to grant a change of venue, improper instructions, insufficient evidence, admission of his statements, and violation of his right to an impartial jury. On review, the court held that the evidence supported the jury's finding of the aggravating circumstance that defendant knowingly created a great risk of death to more than one person, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.11 (1981). The fact that jurors knew the victims did not in itself demonstrate a need for a change of venue. A prospective juror was properly excused based on his view of the death penalty. Defendant's own testimony provided sufficient circumstantial evidence of a breaking under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1431 (1981). Because defendant's evidence of juror misconduct was insufficient to prove actual prejudice, the trial court did not err in denying the motion for a new trial. The jury was properly instructed that they should decide the weight to be given to statements defendant made while partly conscious and while in a weakened state in the hospital if they found that the statements were made freely and voluntarily, without coercion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

Mitchell v. State


No. F-84-497


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 13; 733 P.2d 412; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 292

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. Laurel V. Mitchell, appellant, was convicted of the crime of Possession of Controlled Dangerous Substance, Heroin, After Former Conviction of Two or More Felonies in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Case No. CRF-83-3366. She was sentenced to twenty (20) years imprisonment, and a fine of eight hundred dollars ($800), and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of possession of a controlled dangerous substance, heroin, after former conviction of two or more felonies, and sentenced defendant to 20 years' imprisonment and a fine. OVERVIEW: Defendant was taken to a hospital in an ambulance based on the suspicion of mall security officers that defendant had taken an overdose of drugs. Casey v. State


No. F-84-754


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 12; 732 P.2d 885; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 295



January 21, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 10, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Joe Jennings, District Judge. The appellant, Michael Earl Casey, was convicted in the District Court of Tulsa County, Case No. CRF-83-4377, of Rape in the First Degree and Forcible Sodomy, for which he received sentences of seven and five years' imprisonment, respectively, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action filed by the State of Oklahoma, defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of forcible sodomy under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 888 (1984), and first-degree rape.


OVERVIEW: Officers responded to a call that a man was pushing a woman around outside. Officers found defendant and the victim in defendant's car, the victim performing oral sex on defendant. The victim told the officers that she had been raped. Defendant stated that he had known the victim for more than a year and that she had made such a statement before. The victim testified that defendant offered to give her a ride home but drove her around. She also testified that he raped her in some bushes, and then raped and sodomized her in the vehicle. At the scene, officers saw grass and blood in the car, and a card from the club from which the victim claimed defendant had offered her the ride. Defendant testified that they never had intercourse. Semen was found in the victim. When defendant was initially questioned at the scene, he had not been given Miranda warnings. The court affirmed the judgment. Legislative intent showed that in Oklahoma, forcible sodomy included oral intercourse. The wording, detestable and abominable crime against nature, in § 888 was not indefinite or vague. It was not necessary for defendant to be given Miranda warnings during the initial questioning at the scene.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of forcible sodomy and first-degree rape.

 

929 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Sabo v. State


No. M-85-150


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 10; 732 P.2d 474; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 299



January 21, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 3, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Kay County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Leslie D. Page, District Judge. Edward Harvey Sabo, appellant, was convicted of Driving Under the Influence of Alcohol (Count I) and Leaving the Scene of an Accident Involving Damage to a Motor Vehicle (Count II), in the District Court of Kay County, Case No. CRM-84-372, was sentenced to ninety days' imprisonment in the county jail, a fine of $500 on Count I and $100 on Count II, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  The judgment is AFFIRMED and the sentence is MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of Kay County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of driving under the influence of alcohol and leaving the scene of an accident involving damage to a motor vehicle. He was fined and sentenced to 90 days in the county jail.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol and leaving the scene of an accident involving damage to a motor vehicle. He was fined and sentenced to 90 days in the county jail. On appeal, defendant contended that the statute under which he was convicted for driving under the influence, Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 11-902(A) (1983), was unconstitutionally vague. The court disagreed and held that the statute was constitutional. The court further found that the record was replete with testimony of defendant's legal use of controlled substances sufficient to cause a jury to speculate as to the effects of the substances. It was entirely proper for the trial court to forestall any possible speculation by the jury. Finally, the court found merit in defendant's contention that the acts of which he was convicted fell outside the scope of the Victim's Compensation Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 142.1 (1981). The Victim's Compensation Fund assessments were therefore vacated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences. The court vacated the Victim's Compensation Fund assessments.

 

930 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. F-82-312


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1987 OK CR 8; 731 P.2d 993; 1987 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 290; 74 A.L.R.4th 361



January 16, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 9, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, The Honorable William S. Myers, Jr., District Judge. Malcolm Rent Johnson, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the First Degree in Oklahoma County District Court, Case No. CRF-81-4939. Punishment was assessed as death.



DISPOSITION:  Judgment and sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) for murder in the first degree. Defendant received the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was black, was convicted of killing an elderly woman after brutally raping her. He denied any connection with the crime. The court rejected his numerous allegations of error and upheld his conviction and sentence to death. The court found no error in the exclusion of jurors who were opposed to the death penalty. Their exclusion did not violate defendant's right to a jury composed of a fair cross-section of the community. The prosecutor's use of three peremptory challenges against potential jurors who were black did not violate defendant's right to equal protection because the prosecutor was able to articulate logical, race-neutral reasons for his use of the peremptory challenges. There was no error in the admission of evidence belonging to the victim that was seized during a search of defendant's apartment because his girlfriend who leased the apartment consented to the search. The court held that the jury was not influenced by passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. The evidence of guilt and of the aggravating circumstances necessary for the imposition of the death penalty was substantial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

 

931 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Little v. State


No. F-84-55


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 132; 725 P.2d 606; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 322



September 2, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma The Honorable Karl Gray, District Judge. Warren Warren Little, the appellant, was convicted in Oklahoma County District Court, Case No. CRF-82-6126, of Second Degree Rape and two counts of Sodomy for which he received sentences of fifteen years, ten years, and ten years' imprisonment to run consecutively, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of second degree rape and two counts of sodomy in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981) for which he received sentences of 15 years', 10 years', and 10 years' imprisonment, respectively, to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of sexually abusing his younger stepdaughter, the prosecutrix, and an older stepdaughter testified that defendant had also sexually abused her. Defendant objected to the older stepdaughter's testimony. On appeal, the court found that the testimony was admissible because the testimony showed a common scheme to satisfy his sexual desires. Defendant sexually exploited the stepdaughters in the same progression of acts including attempts to convince the girls that what he was doing was for their benefit and that their mother approved of it. Even if the prosecutrix's testimony contained some inconsistencies, her testimony did not support a reversal of the rape conviction when competent evidence supported the conviction. The older stepdaughter was properly permitted to state that the prosecutrix told her about the events without including details. Section 886 was not unconstitutional because the State had a compelling interest in protecting the physical and mental health of minors who were forced to participate in sexual activity. Defendant's sentence did not shock the court's conscious and, thus, could not be modified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Thompson v. State


No. F-84-29


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 130; 724 P.2d 780; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 318



August 29, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 24, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Grady County, Oklahoma The Honorable James R. Winchester, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the District Court of Grady County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first-degree murder, and his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was certified to stand trial as an adult for his role in the murder of his brother-in-law. The victim was abducted, beaten, and shot. He had his leg broken and his throat slashed before his body was chained to a cement block and thrown in a river. On appeal, appellant objected, inter alia, to the admission of photos as gruesome and prejudicial and claimed his sentence was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The evidence against appellant was so strong that the court could not say that the admission of the photos affected the jury's determination. The imposition of the death penalty on a minor certified to stand trial as an adult was neither cruel nor unusual punishment. The death penalty convictions in which a heinous, atrocious, and cruel aggravating circumstance was found consistently passed constitutional challenges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment of conviction and death sentence.

 

933 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Shockley v. State


No. F-84-647


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 124; 724 P.2d 256; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 317



August 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Hughes County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Gordon R. Melson, District Judge. Joe Riley Shockley, Sr., appellant, was convicted in Hughes County District Court, Case No. CRF-80-80, of Harboring a Fugitive From Justice, was sentenced to seven years' imprisonment, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Hughes County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of harboring a fugitive from justice and sentenced him to seven years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A sheriff and a deputy arrived at defendant's home to talk to defendant's minor son about the shooting of the victim. Defendant stated that his son and his uncle were not in the house, but the officers observed them inside the house and later arrested them after they left the house. Defendant raised several assignments of error. On appeal, the court found that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 440 (1981) was constitutional as applied to defendant, and defendant could not challenge the statute. Defendant intentionally misled the sheriff by denying that his son was in the house when he knew that the sheriff had probable cause to arrest the son. The information charging defendant stated the charge in statutory language, cited the statute, and state sufficient facts to charge a crime; thus, the information was sufficient to withstand defendant's motion to quash. The fact that his son was a minor was irrelevant to charging defendant as an accessory. Any error caused by the prosecutor's remarks that implied that defendant met with his son after the shooting were cured by the trial court's admonishment to counsel to stay within the evidence and were not so prejudicial to require reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

934 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. State


No. F-84-795


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 116; 723 P.2d 273; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 306



July 22, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 25, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Joe Jennings, District Judge. Gary Alan Walker, a/k/a Gary Alan Edwards, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the First Degree, After Former Conviction of Six Felonies, in the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, Case No. CRF-84-2088, sentenced to death, and appeals. AFFIRMED.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which entered a conviction of murder in the first degree, after former conviction of six felonies and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant gave police a detailed confession. when defendant was caught attempting to rob the victim, he killed him with a brick and a vacuum cleaner cord. The court of criminal appeals found that the trial court did not err by refusing to grant a motion for change of venue. Though the issue was properly raised at trial, the court found that defendant was not deprived of due process by the refusal to change venue since, though there was extensive media coverage, considering other factors a venue change was not warranted. Challenges to jury selection were meritless. The jury was not improperly led to believe that the appropriateness of the death penalty rested with an appellate court and no jurors were improperly excused or seated. At trial, defendant raised the insanity defense. The court found that the evidence supported the jury finding that the elements of the crime had been met in spite of the presentation of adequate evidence by defendant in support of his insanity plea. Finally, the court found that the State provided adequate notice of the evidence to be presented and the evidence supported the enhancement of his sentence, resulting in the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court of criminal appeals affirmed defendant's conviction and the application of the death penalty.

 

935 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Casady v. State


No. F-84-251


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 114; 721 P.2d 1342; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 308



July 16, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Custer County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Doug C. Haught, Associate District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the District Court of Custer County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of rape in the first degree, two counts of sodomy, kidnapping, and one count of forcible sodomy, each count being after former conviction of a felony. He received sentences of 100 years in prison on the rape conviction, 150 years on the two sodomy convictions, 100 years on the kidnapping conviction, and 150 years on the forcible sodomy conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant grabbed a victim and forced her in her vehicle. They traveled to an isolated pasture where defendant raped and sodomized the victim a number of times. Defendant was convicted of rape, sodomy, and kidnapping. On appeal, the court affirmed his convictions and his sentences. The statements by the victim's relatives who saw her after the crime were properly admitted because they were relevant. The victim's emotional state indicated that she did not consent to the sexual relations and that the acts described actually occurred. Defendant was not improperly charged with two counts of sodomy under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981) because the statute, which described the forbidden conduct as the detestable and abominable crime against nature, was not unconstitutionally vague. The trial court was not required to call a special overnight recess to examine certain evidence that a State's witness was explaining in court because enlarged copies of fingerprints were not new evidence. It was proper for the State's fingerprint expert to testify at trial because he graphically demonstrated the basis of his conclusion. There was no evidence that the comparison process used was inadequate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

Peninger v. State


No. F-83-626


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 113; 721 P.2d 1338; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 304



July 15, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma The Honorable Joe Cannon, District Judge. Larry Dale Peninger, appellant, was convicted of Kidnapping, Count I; Oral Sodomy, Count II; Anal Sodomy, Count III; and, First Degree Rape, Count IV, in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Case No. CRF-83-246, was sentenced to ten (10) years' imprisonment for Count I; twenty (20) years' imprisonment for Count II; Twenty (20) years' imprisonment for Count III, and seventy-five (75) years' imprisonment for Count IV, each to be served consecutively, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) of the crimes of kidnapping, oral sodomy, anal sodomy, and first-degree rape. Defendant was sentenced to 10 years' imprisonment for the kidnapping conviction, 20 years' imprisonment for each sodomy conviction, and 75 years' imprisonment for the first-degree rape conviction to run consecutively, along with a payment to the Victim's Compensation Fund. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions on the grounds of ineffective assistance of counsel; that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions; that the trial court erroneously instructed the jury; that the prosecutor made inflammatory comments; that the sodomy statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981) was unconstitutionally vague; that his convictions violated his double jeopardy protections; and that the sentences imposed were excessive. The court affirmed the conviction, and modified one of the sentences. The court, after application of the Strickland test, found no merit to the claim of ineffective assistance of counsel, and held that the jury could have found from the evidence that defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant waived his appeal of the jury instructions. The court held that prosecutor's remarks were permissible, and that defendant's constitutional challenge to the statute was meritless. The court held that because each charge required proof that the other charges did not, the single transaction rule was inapplicable. The court modified one of the sentences related to the anal sodomy conviction because of the lack of any mention of force.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions, but modified one of the sentences.

 

937 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Devooght v. State


No. F-84-214


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 100; 722 P.2d 705; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 294



June 25, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma The Honorable John M. Amick, District Judge. James Edward Devooght, III, appellant was convicted in Oklahoma County District Court of Murder in the First Degree, Case No. CRF-83-37. He received a sentence of life imprisonment.



DISPOSITION:  Judgment and sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of murder in the first degree and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a teenager, was tried before a jury for the murder of a six-year-old girl who was found raped and beaten to death in a field near her home. Defendant and his mother, who were staying at the victim's home, were questioned about the girl's disappearance. After the girl's body was found, defendant was arrested and taken to the police station where he made a statement to police. Defendant challenged his murder conviction and sentence, and the court affirmed. The court held that the initial questioning of defendant was not an arrest and did not violate the Fourth Amendment. Defendant's arrest was legal because probable cause was established, and his inculpatory statements were properly admitted. The charging information was not unconstitutionally vague, and the jury represented a fair and impartial cross-section of the community even though those who could not impose the death penalty were removed for cause. The trial court did not err in admitting into evidence the hearsay statements of the victim's four-year-old sister because she was unavailable as a witness due to her age and the trustworthiness of the statements was supported by corroborating evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Rogers v. State


No. F-83-742


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 96; 721 P.2d 805; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 284



June 24, 1986, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 1, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma The Honorable Joe Cannon, District Judge. Gary Lamont Rogers, appellant, was convicted of the crime of Rape in the Second Degree, in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Case No. CRF-82-4913. He was sentenced to a term of nine (9) years imprisonment, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of rape in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judge's decision to refuse defendant's motion for certification as a juvenile. Under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2, the trial court was vested with the discretion to certify defendant as a juvenile. The court found this statute was not unconstitutional. The court disregarded the issue as to whether the judge abused his discretion in overruling the motion to certify defendant as a juvenile because counsel failed to supply the court with an adequate record to review the issue. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's request for a continuance of the trial date. Defendant's argument that the trial court improperly refused admission of extrinsic evidence proving a prior inconsistent statement by the victim was patently frivolous. Because there was no authority cited by defendant to support a claim that the admission at trial of evidence seized by the city police was erroneous, the court rejected that claim. Finally, defendant was not denied his Sixth Amendment right to effective assistance of counsel because although defendant's counsel ignored various rules of evidence, the errors and conduct of counsel did not affect the outcome of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

939 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Swart v. State


No. C-84-584


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 92; 720 P.2d 1265; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 282



June 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma The Honorable Jay Dalton, District Judge. The Honorable Jay Dalton, District Judge. Thomas Deshawn Swart, appellant, was convicted of Attempted Burglary and Knowingly Concealing Stolen Property, in the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, Case No. CRF-84-114 and CRF-84-178, sentenced to thirty (30) months and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED and REMANDED for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) convicting him of attempted burglary and knowingly concealing stolen property. Defendant was sentenced to 30 months imprisonment pursuant to the Oklahoma Intermediate Offender Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 995 et seq. (Supp. 1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in two separate cases with the crimes of attempted burglary and knowingly concealing stolen property. Defendant appeared for arraignment and indicated his wish to plead guilty to a 30-month negotiated sentence. The trial court, though expressing his doubts concerning the constitutionality of the Act, ruled the Act had application to his case, and that defendant would be sentenced accordingly. Defendant filed a petition for an extraordinary writ with the court, which was denied. Defendant subsequently entered his pleas of guilty to each offense. Despite the State's recommendation of a 30-month determinate sentence on each offense, the trial court sentenced defendant to an indeterminate sentence. The central issue presented on appeal was the constitutionality of the Act. The court determined that the classification created by the Act did not violate a fundamental right and that the Act bore a rational relation to a legitimate state interest. Despite the meritorious and otherwise constitutional purposes of the Act, the court held that the Act violated the separation of powers provision found in Okla. Const. art. IV, § 1, and was unconstitutional on that basis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause for resentencing.

 

940 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Staggs v. State


No. M-84-530


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 88; 719 P.2d 1297; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 279



June 10, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Beckham County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Gary P. McGinn, District Judge. David Mack Staggs, appellant, was convicted of the crime of Driving Under the Influence of Alcohol, in the District Court of Beckham County, Case No. CRM-83-605. He was sentenced to a term of six (6) months in prison, and a fine of five hundred dollars ($500), and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the District Court of Beckham County (Oklahoma) that convicted him of driving under the influence of alcohol and sentenced him to a fine and a term of six months in prison.


OVERVIEW: After arresting defendant, a police officer attempted to administer a breathalyzer test. He testified that he terminated the test because defendant was uncooperative in that he stopped blowing into the machine and drew his breath back in each time the machine's green light came on. Defendant testified that he consented to the test, and he denied that he had been drinking or that he was uncooperative. The court affirmed the judgment. Whether defendant was provided with an opportunity to take a valid test was a question for the jury. Although the evidence of defendant's failure to cooperate was elicited by defendant's counsel during cross-examination, the court refused to permit defendant to profit from his own error in eliciting incompetent evidence. The presentence investigation statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 982 (Supp. 1983) was not unconstitutional in ordering presentence investigations only in the case of felonies. It did not prohibit trial judges from ordering such investigations in misdemeanor cases, and the distinction was logically related to the longer sentences imposed for felonies. Defendant's punishment was within the framework established by law and was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Reed v. State


No. F-84-594


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 64; 718 P.2d 373; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 251



April 29, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Okmulgee County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Charles Humphrey, Special Judge. Richard R. Reed, appellant, was convicted of the crime of Making Lewd or Indecent Proposals to a Child Under Sixteen, in the District Court of Okmulgee County, Case No. CRF-83-237. He was sentenced to two (2) years imprisonment, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Okmulgee County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of making lewd or indecent proposals to a child under 16 and sentenced him to two years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: While the 15-year-old victim walked to school, defendant, whom she had met before, offered her a ride. Defendant began kissing the victim without her consent. He told the victim that he wanted to make love to her. Defendant continued to kiss the victim, unbuttoned her pants, and placed his hand on her leg. The victim fled to a neighbor's house. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for making lewd or indecent proposals to a child under 16. The statement that "I want to make love to you" was an oral lewd or indecent proposal to have unlawful sexual relations within the purview of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1123 (1983). The phrase was commonly understood as referring to sexual intercourse. The court also found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The statute was identical to a prior statute except that it provided protection to minors of an older age than the prior statute. Nor was the statute overbroad or violative of the guarantee of free speech, as the court had addressed the issue of whether the prior statute was overbroad and violative of the guarantee of free speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Palmer v. State


No. F-83-13


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 62; 719 P.2d 1285; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 250



April 25, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Charles L. Owens, District Judge. Robert Dean Palmer, appellant, was convicted of Manslaughter in the First Degree and sentence to fifty years' imprisonment in the District Court of Oklahoma County, in Case No. CRF-82-984, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Judgment and Sentence AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of manslaughter in the first degree. The jury being unable to agree on the sentence, the trial court sentenced defendant to 50 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went into a nursing home and stabbed on the residents six times. Defendant had been drinking heavily and had smoked a marijuana cigarette offered by someone else prior to the crime. An expert testified that defendant's symptoms after smoking the marijuana were consistent with those who have taken PCP. Defendant sought an instruction on involuntary intoxication alleging the marijuana cigarette was laced with PCP. The trial court denied the requested instruction and also denied a request for a character instruction. Defendant was convicted. The court affirmed finding that the intoxicated condition of defendant was his own doing. The court noted that the jury took into consideration defendant's condition even without the instruction being given as evidenced by the fact that they did not convict him of first degree murder. The court held that the trial court's error in failing to give defendant's requested instruction on evidence of his character was harmless. The court found the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting photos depicting the lower regions of the victim's body with a stab wound to the right of the vaginal area.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of first degree manslaughter, and his sentence to fifty years imprisonment, were affirmed.

 

943 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Post v. State


No. F-84-303


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 52; 717 P.2d 1151; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 237



April 14, 1986, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State of Oklahoma sought a rehearing of the court's opinion, specifically challenging the court's resolution regarding the unconstitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981) as applied to the facts of the case against appellant. The State claimed that the court's opinion was in conflict with previous rulings of the United States Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: In denying the petition for rehearing, the court pointed out that the cases cited by the State upheld statutes against a claim of being constitutionally vague, and that it had held that § 886 was not unconstitutionally vague. The court also rejected the application of another Supreme Court case cited by the State, noting that in that case, which involved the constitutionality of applying a state sodomy statute to homosexuals, the plaintiffs had neither been arrested nor threatened with prosecution. Although the summary affirmance of the lower court's decision in that case was dispositive of the merits and had binding precedential effect, the court held that an affirmance by a court that did not explain its reasons was not an endorsement of the reasoning employed by the lower court, and the summary holding was required to be carefully limited. The court noted that the Supreme Court may have disposed of that case on the basis that the plaintiffs clearly lacked standing to bring the lawsuit. Accordingly, any reliance on that case by the court would have been improper.


OUTCOME: The court denied the State's petition for rehearing. The court stayed the mandate to provide the state with an opportunity to file a petition for a writ of certiorari with the United States Supreme Court.

 

944 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Cent. Ambulance Serv. v. City of Tulsa


No. M-83-646


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 46; 716 P.2d 705; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 233



April 4, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the Municipal Court of the City of Tulsa, Oklahoma The Honorable Laurence A. Yeagley, Presiding Judge. Central Ambulance Service, Inc., appellant, was convicted of Operating an Ambulance for Hire within the Tulsa Corporate Limits on Routine Transfers without a Valid Permit (2 charges), in the Municipal Court of the City of Tulsa, Case Nos. CORP-82-2 and CORP-82-3, was sentenced to $100 and costs on both charges, and it appeals. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a corporation, appealed from a judgment of the Municipal Court of the City of Tulsa, Oklahoma, which convicted it of two counts of operating an ambulance for hire within the city's limits on routine transfers without a valid permit and imposed a fine and costs on both charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Tulsa, Okla., Rev. Ordinances tit. 37, ch. 13, §§ 501-525 (1978), which regulated the city's ambulance service, was unconstitutional. Defendant possessed a state ambulance service license, but the state excluded non-emergency transfers from licensure. The city did not. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, finding that the city had the authority under its police power granted to it by the state to regulate ambulance service within its jurisdiction. State licensure was not a factor. The court found that the ordinances in question were not an abuse of the city's power because the standards imposed by the city were reasonable. The court noted that defendant was not being denied a property right because it had not applied for the license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Wood v. State


No. F-84-815


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 47; 716 P.2d 707; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 240

Lawrence Douglas Wood, appellant, was convicted of the crime of Operating a Motor Vehicle While Having a Blood or Breath Alcohol Concentration of Ten-Hundredths (0.10) or More After Former Conviction, in the District.Court of Oklahoma County, Case No. CRF-83-4582. He was sentenced to a term of five (5) years imprisonment, and appeals. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for operating a motor vehicle while having a blood or breath alcohol concentration of .10 or more after former conviction from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma).


OVERVIEW: An officer observed defendant fail to use a turn indicators, suspected defendant was intoxicated, and administered a breathalyzer test. Defendant was convicted at trial. The court stated that this contention was patently frivolous. The court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court improperly limited counsel's right to cross-examine the officer administering the breathalyzer test as to his ability to identify defendant. The court explained that where several other witnesses had made a positive identification, the trial court's limitations were neither an abuse of discretion, nor prejudicial. Finally, the court rejected defendant's claim that Okla. Stat. tit. 47, 11-902(A)(1) (1982) was unconstitutional and void for vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Post v. State


No. F-84-303


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 30; 715 P.2d 1105; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 213



February 26, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 14, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Rogers County, Oklahoma The Honorable Byron Ed Williams, District Judges. James Lester Post, Jr., appellant, was convicted of two counts of Crime Against Nature, and Maiming, in the District Court of Rogers County, Oklahoma, Case No. CRF-83-17, sentenced to ten years on each of the two counts of Crime Against Nature, and fifteen (15) years on the count of Maiming.



DISPOSITION:  The convictions are REVERSED and REMANDED for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed orders from the District Court of Rogers County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of two counts of crimes against nature, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981), and one count of maiming. Defendant was sentenced to 10 years imprisonment on each of the counts of crimes against nature and 15 years on the count of maiming, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 751 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The victim asserted that defendant forced her, at knifepoint, to have sex with him and sodomized her. The victim also asserted that defendant beat her, causing severe injury to her eye. Defendant asserted that the sexual acts were consensual. Defendant stated that he hit the victim because he thought she was robbing him. Defendant was charged with rape, crimes against nature, and maiming. At trial, the victim's doctor testified that her eye was highly susceptible to injury due to previous damage. The jury acquitted defendant of rape and asked for further instruction on consent to crimes against nature. The trial judge instructed the jury that consent was not an element of crimes against nature. On appeal, the court reversed the crimes against nature conviction because the charge was unconstitutional as applied to defendant. Recent U.S. Supreme Court case law had indicated that the right to privacy prevented government regulation of sexual activity between consenting adults, even though unmarried. The trial court erred by refusing to instruct on the lesser-included offenses of assault and battery when his explanation for the injury indicated a lack of specific intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for two counts of crimes against nature and one count of maiming. The court remanded for a new trial on the charges.

Foster v. State


No. F-84-76


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 19; 714 P.2d 1031; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 203



February 4, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 17, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Muskogee County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Lyle Burris, Associate District Judge. Charles A. Foster, appellant was convicted in Muskogee County District Court, Case No. CRF-83-194, of Burglary in the Second Degree, Larceny of an Automobile, and Grand Larceny, each After Former Conviction of Two Felonies, and of Murder in the First Degree. He received sentences of ninety years' imprisonment for each of the first three convictions and the death penalty for murder.



DISPOSITION:  Judgments and sentences are AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with burglary in the second degree, larceny of an automobile, grand larceny, each after former conviction of two felonies, and murder in the first degree. The District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma) convicted him of each count after a trial by jury. He received sentences of 90 years' imprisonment for each of the first three convictions and the death penalty for murder.


OVERVIEW: The 74-year-old victim owned a grocery store and made local deliveries. The night he was killed, he had made a delivery to defendant's home. While waiting for defendant's wife to return with payment for the groceries, according to the wife's testimony, defendant suddenly started accusing the victim of having "something to do" with his wife, pushing him and then striking him with a baseball bat. Defendant left for an hour and a half, wrapped the victim, who was still breathing, in a blanket, and left in the victim's car. The couple then fled Oklahoma in the victim's car. Defendant had in his possession a number of the victim's household items. The jury convicted defendant. The court affirmed. Introduction of a bat similar to the bat used was not prejudicial. The State was careful to inform the jury that the bat was not the weapon used, but only a likeness. Prejudice from exposure to adverse pretrial publicity was not shown. Defendant was not entitled to a jury composed of those who would not follow the law or whose views concerning the death penalty would have tainted their impartiality. The presence of all three aggravating circumstances was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the sentences.

Henager v. State


No. F-83-436


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 20; 716 P.2d 669; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 205



February 4, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended February 7, 1986..


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma The Honorable Alan J. Couch, District Judge. Harold Richard Henager, appellant, was convicted of Feloniously Pointing a Weapon, After Former Conviction of a Felony, and Second Degree Burglary, After Former Conviction of a Felony, in the District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma, Case Nos. CRF-81-519 and CRF-81-520, sentenced to twenty (20) years' imprisonment for each case with sentences to run concurrently, and he appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma) for burglary in the second degree after former conviction of a felony in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1435 (1981) and feloniously pointing a weapon after former conviction of a felony in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1289.16 (1981).


OVERVIEW: As the victim approached his mobile home, an assailant pointed a weapon at him before fleeing. The mobile home had been ransacked. The victim identified defendant as his assailant during a photographic line-up conducted four days later. Defendant's trial was delayed due to his incarceration in a federal facility in another state. On appeal, defendant asserted numerous allegations of error, which were all rejected by the court in affirming his convictions. Defendant made two challenges to the delay in bringing his case to trial. The court held that defendant was tried within the 180-day period provided in Article III (a),(b),(c) of the Interstate Agreement on Detainers, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1347 (1981), because the 180-period did not begin until the State filed its detainer. By agreeing to a continuance, defendant consented to the tolling of the time period. Defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a speedy trial was not violated by the 484-day lapse in the filing of the information and the date of trial. Defendant was partially responsible for the delay. As for prejudice, he failed to offer proof to support his allegations of the deaths of two witnesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Harris v. State


No. C-84-346


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 13; 713 P.2d 601; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 200



January 28, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Bryan County, Oklahoma The Honorable Billy A. Mickle, Associate District Judge. Mitchell Harris, appellant, was convicted of First Degree Burglary, AFCF, First Degree Burglary, AFCF, and Forcible Sodomy, AFCF, in the District Court of Bryan County, Case Nos. CRF-83-326, CRF-83-325, and CRF-83-324, was sentenced to forty (40) years' imprisonment in each case, and he appeals. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment by the District Court of Bryan County (Oklahoma) convicting him, upon his guilty plea, of first degree burglary and forcible sodomy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant advised the trial court that he wanted to change his pleas to guilty. The trial judge very carefully examined defendant. Later, defendant filed an application to withdraw his guilty pleas within the time allowed. He was given a hearing at which the only evidence he offered was his own testimony which was an impeachment of his own prior testimony. Defendant had the burden of proving that his guilty plea was not voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently entered. However, the court found that he did not meet that burden. Defendant also claimed that the two prior convictions arose out of the same transaction or occurrence or series of events. Thus, he contended that Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 51(B) (1981) was not applicable. This issue was not raised at the trial level, and the court found that there was no evidence that the two prior convictions were related incidents. The case numbers were not even close numerically. The fact that the convictions were entered on the same date and the sentences were ordered to run concurrently did not mean that the cases were related in the sense described in § 51(B). Thus, the court found that this claim was groundless.


OUTCOME: Defendant's judgment of conviction for first degree burglary and forcible sodomy was affirmed.

 

950 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Howard v. City of Tulsa


No. M-83-783


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 5; 712 P.2d 797; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 193



January 7, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 6, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Tulsa Municipal Court The Honorable John S. Turner, Municipal Judge.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision from the Tulsa Municipal Court (Oklahoma), which convicted him of disturbing the peace and fined him accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, while conducting outdoor religious revivals during which loud music was played, was cited for disturbing the peace after having been previously warned about the disturbance. The cite came under the City of Tulsa Rev. Ordinances tit. 27, § 401(B), which prohibited the willful or malicious disturbance of the peace. Appellant was convicted and he appealed, contending that the ordinance was vague and overbroad, and unduly restricted the free exercise of his religion. On review the court noted that it was well within the City's discretion to regulate noise disturbances. Furthermore, the freedom of speech privilege was not an absolute privilege. The court noted that the ordinance gave fair warning of the nature of the proscribed act and the ordinance regulated the time, place, and manner of the expression, which was a legitimate regulation as it furthered significant government interests, i.e., maintaining the peace. The court also noted that the challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence was better left to the trier of fact, and the fact that appellant was in charge of the revival subjected him to the punishment as a principal, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 432 (1981).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence.

Hicks v. State


No. F-83-263


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1986 OK CR 7; 713 P.2d 18; 1986 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 194



January 7, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 15, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, The Honorable Jay Dalton, District Judge. Troy Lee Hicks, appellant, was convicted of Sodomy and Burglary in the First Degree, in Tulsa County District Court, Case No. CRF-82-1394, was sentenced to three (3) years and seven (7) years respectively, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Burglary in the First Degree judgment and sentence is AFFIRMED; Sodomy judgment and sentence is REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for sodomy in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981), and burglary in the first degree in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1431 (1981), entered on a jury verdict by the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, which sentenced him to three years and seven years respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981) was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court agreed but based on previous precedent held that the constitutional claim was without merit. However, the court reversed the conviction for sodomy based on the finding that the State had failed proving the essential element of penetration. The court ruled that under Okla. Stat. tit. X, § x (1981), the sodomy crime required sexual penetration, however slight. The court also held that the record showed that the child witness had been able to distinguish truth from fiction and was sworn under oath. The testimony had demonstrated her personal knowledge of the crime against her mother. The trial court's questions of the witness were proper and within its authority for interrogating a witness. An interpreter for the child, a deaf-mute, was not sworn, but defendant's right to have had the interpreter sworn under oath was waived. The right was waived because he knew and failed to object and also because he had not shown by direct examination or independent testimony that the interpretations were incorrect. Any error in prosecutorial comment had not affected the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's judgment and sentence for burglary in the first degree and reversed the judgment and sentence for sodomy.

Green v. State


Nos. F-81-797


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1985 OK CR 126; 713 P.2d 1032; 1985 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 302



October 9, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 24, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Pittsburg County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Robert A. Layden, District Judge. MICHAEL WAYNE GREEN an DANNY GEORGE PARKER, appellants, were convicted of Murdr in the First Degree in violation of 21 O.S.1981, § 701.7, in the District Court of Pittsburg County, Oklahoma, Case No. F-81-120, sentenced to death by lethal injection, and appeal.



DISPOSITION:  The sentence of appellant Green is AFFIRMED; and the sentence of appellant Parker is MODIFIED to life imprisonment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the District Court of Pittsburg County, Oklahoma, which entered a jury verdict convicting them of murder in the first degree and sentenced defendants to death by lethal drug injection.


OVERVIEW: The evidence revealed that defendants, both of who were serving lengthy prison terms, brutally stabbed and killed another inmate with a butcher knife and a homemade weapon. A jury convicted each defendant of murder in the first degree. The trial court sentenced defendants to death by lethal drug injection. The court affirmed the convictions, but reversed the death penalty for one defendant. The evidence was insufficient to support the aggravated circumstance that one defendant had been previously convicted of a felony involving the use or threat of violence to the person under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.12(1) (1981). That defendant's previous convictions for escape and kidnapping did not, without any other proof, show that he used or threatened force to commit these acts. A pre-accusation delay did not implicate the requirement of a speedy trial. Defendants did not show that they suffered actual prejudice by the delay to implicate the Due Process Clause. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendants' motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence where another inmate's confession to the murder was inconsistent with other evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting each defendant of murder in the first degree. The court affirmed the death penalty for one defendant, but modified the sentence of the other defendant to life imprisonment.

In re L.G.M.


Case No. J-84-129


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1985 OK CR 97; 704 P.2d 88; 1985 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 265



July 30, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 30, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Rogers County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Edwin D. Carden, District Judge. L.G.M., Jr., a Delinquent child, was adjudicated a delinquent child in the District Court of Rogers County, Oklahoma, Case No. J-83-45, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor was adjudicated delinquent in the District Court of Rogers County (Oklahoma) and sought review. The minor argued that the initial stop and search was without probable cause, that the trial court erred in failing to suppress the seized items, and that Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1344 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The minor was stopped in a store by a clerk and when she searched his bag, she discovered store merchandise that had not been paid for. The minor argued that there was no probable cause for the search and the seized items should have been suppressed. The court affirmed the adjudication and held that while the clerk did not have probable cause to stop him, the evidence was admissible. The court held that the constitutional protection from search and seizures did not apply to a private action. The court found that neither Okla. Stat. tit. 22, §§ 1343 nor 1344 provided any exclusionary sanction when the statute was violated. The court also held that § 1344 was not unconstitutional and it did not create a presumption of probable cause in favor of the State if the accused individual was found in possession of stolen merchandise. The court found that the statute provided a presumption to protect the merchant from civil or criminal prosecution for false imprisonment. The court also held that it was not error for the trial court to allow the State to reopen its case to introduce the seized merchandise particularly since a prima facie case of delinquency had been established.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the minor's delinquency adjudication.

Wooten v. State


No. F-82-768


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1985 OK CR 71; 702 P.2d 59; 1985 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 244



June 19, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Muskogee County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Bill Ed Rogers, District Judge. Galen Rodney Wooten, appellant, was convicted of Bringing Alcoholic Beverages Into a Penal Institution, After Former Conviction of a Felony, in the District Court of Muskogee, Oklahoma, Case No. CRF-82-768, sentenced to ten years, and appeals. As Modified, Affirmed.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of bringing alcoholic beverages into a penal institution after former conviction of a felony and sentenced him to 10 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an inmate serving a sentence in prison, was convicted of bringing alcoholic beverages into a penal institution and sentenced to 10 years imprisonment. On appeal, defendant argued that AFCF enhancement was inappropriate because a former felony conviction was implicit in Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 21, and that the trial judge misunderstood the law in regard to whether sentence should run concurrently or consecutively with the sentence then being served. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that § 21 applied to inmates and non-inmates alike and therefore that there was no implied former felony conviction in the statute. The court further held that because the sentence then being served had already been passed when defendant was subsequently convicted for bringing alcohol into the prison, the trial judge properly concluded that he lacked the authority to order that the sentence run concurrently with the sentence then being served. The court modified the sentence to three years imprisonment, holding that the 10 year sentence shocked the conscience of the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of bringing alcoholic beverages into a penal institution after former conviction of a felony. The court modified the sentence to three years imprisonment and to run consecutively with any sentences then being served.

Clem v. State


Case No. M-83-188


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1985 OK CR 66; 701 P.2d 770; 1985 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 230



June 10, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 3, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Dewey County, Oklahoma. The Honorable R. W. Collier, Associate District Judge. Sandra Clem, appellant, was found in direct contempt of court in the District Court of Dewey County, Case No. C-82-230, and she appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction from the District Court of Dewey County (Oklahoma) for direct contempt of court.


OVERVIEW: A grand jury was convened to investigate thefts of oil and oil field equipment. The grand jury subpoenaed defendant, an employee of a company under investigation. Defendant appeared before the grand jury and exercised her Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination. The State offered, and the trial court granted, immunity to her. Defendant persisted in her refusal to answer questions. Defendant was held in contempt of court. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the order of contempt resulted from defendant's refusal to testify after a grant of immunity, not from the method by which the trial court decided the validity of her self-incrimination claim. Also, the grand jury was not convened by the District Attorney; it was convened by the District Judge, at the District Attorney's request, pursuant to the court's authority under the Oklahoma Constitution. Nothing precluded a District Attorney from making such a request. Testimony could properly be compelled from a witness in state proceedings regardless of the Fifth Amendment privilege, if there was immunity from federal and state use of the compelled testimony in any subsequent prosecution of the witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for direct contempt of court. Defendant's request for oral argument was denied.

1985 OK CR 65; 701 P.2d 765; 1985 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 232

Tommy Dale Glass, appellant, was convicted of two counts of First Degree Rape, two counts of Crime Against Nature, two counts of Robbery With a Dangerous Weapon, and one count of Assault With Intent to Rape in violation of 21 O.S.1981, §§ 681, 801, 886 and 1114, in the District Court of Comanche County, Case No. CRF-82-318, sentenced to one-hundred-nine (109) years, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.

OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion for severance of offenses because the information fatally misjoined seven separate offenses involving three distinct incidents of criminal activity. (1981).The court noted that the offenses occurred over a relatively short period of time, in approximately the same location, and proof as to each transaction overlapped so as to evidence a common scheme or plan. The court said that while the prosecutor's conduct was inappropriate, prejudicial error did not occur. Finally, the court rejected defendant's claim that the convictions for the crime against nature could not stand because the statute prohibiting such acts, Okla. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for one count of assault with intent to rape, two counts of first-degree rape, two counts of crime against nature, and two counts of robbery with a dangerous weapon.

Banks v. State


Case No. F-81-179


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1985 OK CR 60; 701 P.2d 418; 1985 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 235



May 30, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Joe Jennings, District Judge. Anthony Rozelle Banks, appellant, was convicted of First Degree Murder, in the Tulsa County District Court, Case No. CRF-79-3393, was sentenced to death, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction on charges by the State for first-degree murder and his sentence of death by lethal injection under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1014 (1981) by the Tulsa County District Court (Oklahoma) on grounds of the unconstitutionality of the death penalty statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981).


OVERVIEW: In a joint trial, defendant was convicted of the first-degree murder of a store clerk, which was committed in the course of a robbery with his co-defendant.
