No abuse of discretion by the trial court occurred that was related to the admittance of evidence at trial or during sentencing. In the sentencing phase of defendant's trial, evidence of aggravating circumstances was admitted in compliance with Okla. Stat. tit. 21, §§ 701.10, 701.12(5) (1981) and the penalty of death was proportionate under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13 (1981) to the penalty imposed in similar cases.

Golden v. State


No. F-83-584


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1985 OK CR 9; 695 P.2d 6; 1985 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 236



January 20, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Greer County; William Fancher, Associate District Judge. Louis Daniel Golden, appellant, was convicted of the Crime Against Nature (Sodomy), in the District Court of Greer County, Case No. CFR-82-17, was sentenced to five years imprisonment, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by information in the District Court of Greer County (Oklahoma) with the crime against nature (sodomy), pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981). Defendant waived his right to a trial by jury, and was convicted and sentenced to five years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim, a 13-year old boy, stated that he had arranged with defendant to mow a lawn. After he and defendant arrived at the location, they went inside the house. Defendant forced the victim onto a mattress, unsnapped the boy's pants, and placed the boy's penis inside his mouth. The bot ran away, and the police were notified. Defendant admitted that he and the boy went into the house, but denied the rest of the account. The court denied defendant's contention that Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1981) was unconstitutionally vague, citing to the theory of stare decisis. The court found that the evidence supported the trial court's finding that defendant engaged in unlawful oral copulation with the victim, in violation of § 886 and Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 887 (1981).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment and sentence.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

Brogie v. State


No. F-80-553


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1985 OK CR 2; 695 P.2d 538; 1985 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 170



January 2, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 4, 1985; Rehearing Denied March 8, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Alma B. Wilson, District Judge. Kirk Wayne Brogie, appellant, was convicted of First Degree Murder in Cleveland County District Court, Case No. CRF-79-640 and was sentenced to death, the Honorable Alma B. Wilson, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  On appeal, the judgment and sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant for first-degree felony murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for first-degree felony murder for his role in an incident in which he and three accomplices kidnapped, raped, and killed the victim by repeatedly stabbing and striking her on the head. Defendant was sentenced to death for his conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence. The court held that: (1) the trial court's refusal to appoint a psychiatrist was proper because there was not statutory or constitutional right to have one appointed; (2) there was sufficient evidence to support the aggravating circumstance that the crime was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel; (3) evidence of the burning of the victim's car was properly admitted because it part of the murder transaction and evidence regarding the plot to kill one of the accomplices was admissible to show efforts to destroy evidence; (4) the trial court's exclusion of a juror opposed to the death penalty was proper; (5) it was not an error for the trial judge to request that the jury reach a verdict; (6) the trial court's exclusion of the sentences received by accomplices was not an error; and (7) imposition of the death penalty was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of first-degree felony murder and sentenced him to death.

 

962 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bowen v. State


No. F-81-315


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1984 OK CR 105; 715 P.2d 1093; 1984 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 218



November 30, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 8, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Raymond Naifeh, District Judge. Clifford Henry Bowen, appellant, was convicted of three (3) counts of Murder in the First Degree, in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Case No. CRF-80-3397. He was sentenced to death on each count, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, which convicted him on three counts of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death on each count. Defendant's claim for a retrial based on newly discovered evidence was denied after an evidentiary hearing to determine the merit of his motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that it was a scientific impossibility to travel from the location where alibi witnesses saw him to the scene of the homicides within 45 minutes. Further, he claimed that the State announced this evidence on the last day of the trial, thereby depriving him of an opportunity to properly respond. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the issue was not whether the defense had knowledge prior to trial with regard to an intention to present this airplane theory on rebuttal. Rather, the question was whether defendant could not with reasonable diligence have discovered the new evidence before the trial, the standard under 22 Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 952 (1981). Moreover, the evidence defendant attempted to present was merely to impeach the State's witness as to the technical possibilities of travel within the time parameters. The court held that this type of evidence was not sufficient to warrant a new trial. Finally, under the materiality requirements of § 952, defendant failed to show that any undisclosed information might have helped the defense or might have affected the outcome of the trial does not establish.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentences to death.

Nuckols v. State


Case No. F-83-153


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1984 OK CR 92; 690 P.2d 463; 1984 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 206



October 19, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 15, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Pottawatomie County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Lloyd H. Henry, District Judge. Kenneth Franklin Nuckols, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the First Degree, in the District Court of Pottawatomie County, in Case No. CRF-83-273, sentenced to death, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the District Court of Pottawatomie County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of murder in the first degree and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a friend stopped on an interstate to purportedly give aid to the motorist. The friend repaired the motorist's car, and defendant and the friend invited the motorist to have a beer. Defendant hit the motorist in the head with a ball peen hammer, and defendant and his friend beat and killed the motorist. Defendant challenged his murder conviction and death sentence, but the court affirmed. The court held that no constitutional violation occurred regarding defendant's confession. Since defendant's motion to suppress the statement based on the denial of the right to counsel revolved around a factual question determined adversely to defendant by the lower court, it was not disturbed on appeal in light of the sufficient evidence presented. There was a legitimate security reason for separating defendant from the main jail population, and defendant's statements were not a product of coercion by the police. Photographs of the motorist victim's head and face were properly entered as evidence. The circumstances leading up to, and the manner in which the homicide was committed, were sufficiently atrocious aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence and judgment of the lower court.

 

964 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Eddings v. State


No. C-78-325


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


688 P.2d 342; 1984 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 207



October 12, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 688 P.2d 342 at 346.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of July 30, 1984, Reported at: 688 P.2d 342.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition with the court and urged the court to overrule Johnson v. State and reinstate a sentence of death, or, in the alternative, to apply a rational basis analysis and distinguish Johnson v. State, a case tried by jury, from judge-tried cases.


OVERVIEW: The State urged the court to overrule Johnson v. State, 665 P.2d 815 (Okla. Cr. 1983) and reinstate a sentence of death, or, in the alternative, to apply a rational basis analysis and distinguish Johnson, a case tried by jury, from judge-tried cases. The court declined to do either. When the court handed down its decision in Johnson, the Oklahoma Legislature was still in session. The Oklahoma Legislature could have then, or in its most recent session, enacted a procedure for resentencing had it felt that the Court had misinterpreted the legislative intent. The Oklahoma Legislature did not do that. Thus, the court had to conclude that the Johnson interpretation was correct and that the court carried out the clear legislative intent. The court's decision upon rehearing Johnson was therefore reaffirmed.


OUTCOME: The court denied the State's request, and the sentence of death was modified.

 

965 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Clayton v. State


No. F-81-590


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1984 OK CR 88; 695 P.2d 3; 1984 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 202



September 7, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 28, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable David M. Cook, District Judge. BARRY C. CLAYTON, appellant, was convicted in separate counts of Attempted Oral Sodomy and Burglary in the First Degree, and was sentenced to three (3) years' imprisonment and fifteen (15) years' imprisonment respectively on those convictions.



DISPOSITION:  He appeals and the judgments and sentences are AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted oral sodomy in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, §§ 44 and 886 (1981) and first degree burglary in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1431 (1981) in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma). On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in binding him over for trial and in overruling his demurrer to the State's evidence, and that Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal that the trial court erred in denying him another preliminary hearing after the State amended the information. The court held that the transcript of the hearing reflected that the trial judge found that the evidence was sufficient to bind defendant over for trial. Defendant also argued that the trial court improperly admitted certain State's exhibits that the court held was proper because the State had laid the proper foundation prior to the trial judge questioning a witness about them. The court held that the trial court properly overruled defendant's demurrer to the State's evidence because once defendant presented evidence in his own defense, the demurrer was waived and because there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's verdict. Further, the court held that § 886 was not unconstitutionally vague because the statutory language "detestable and abominable crime against nature" had been defined by prior court decisions to include oral sodomy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

966 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Eddings v. State


No. C-78-325


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1984 OK CR 79; 688 P.2d 342; 1984 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 191



July 30, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 12, 1984, Reported at: 688 P.2d 342 at 346.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Creek County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Charles Woodson, District Judge. Monty Lee Eddings, appellant, was convicted of the crime of Murder in the First Degree in Case No. CRF-77-118, in the District Court of Creek County, Oklahoma. He appealed. AFFIRMED. On appeal to the United States Supreme Court for Writ of Certiorari the case was REVERSED IN PART and REMANDED for further proceedings. Appellant sought issuance of a writ of prohibition to prevent hearing. DENIED. Further evidence heard on remand and appellant again sentenced to death.



DISPOSITION:  MODIFIED to life imprisonment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of Creek County (Oklahoma) of first degree murder and sentenced to death. On his direct appeal, the court affirmed his conviction and sentence after which, by writ of certiorari, the United States Supreme Court reversed in part and remanded the cause for further proceedings. The court remanded the cause to the trial court, which again sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed from his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant waived a jury trial and entered a plea of nolo contendre. The trial court imposed the death sentence, which the court affirmed. On certiorari, the Supreme Court reversed the affirmance of the death penalty because both the trial court and the court had improperly placed limitations upon the mitigating circumstances to be considered. The Supreme Court directed the courts to consider all relevant mitigating evidence and weigh it against the aggravating circumstances. Because the court did not weigh evidence, remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. The trial court heard additional evidence and again imposed the death penalty. On appeal, the court held that it was error for it to remand to the trial court for resentencing and that the death sentence had to be modified to life imprisonment because when prejudicial error occurred in the sentencing stage of the trial only, the court had consistently modified the death sentence to life imprisonment. Because the court was without authority to remand jury-tried cases for resentencing, it also had to modify to life imprisonment cases where the trial court erred in imposing the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court modified defendant's sentence from death to life imprisonment.

Rushing v. State


No. F-81-206


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1984 OK CR 39; 676 P.2d 842; 1984 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 143



January 24, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 24, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Motions for New Trial upon Newly Discovered Evidence from the District Court of Garfield County, Oklahoma. The Honorable W.O. Green, III., Judge. Jerry R. Rushing, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the First Degree, in the District Court of Garfield County, Oklahoma, Case No. CRF-80-13. He was sentenced to life imprisonment and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Motions for New Trial OVERRULED and judgment and sentence AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Garfield County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of the offense of murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant also filed two motions for new trial upon newly discovered evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant attempted to establish that an accomplice in a related offense killed the victim and that he was not involved in the murder. He contended on appeal, inter alia, that the trial court's evidentiary rulings created reversible error. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence and overruled the motions for new trial, and held that (1) Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 742 (1981) provided that a conviction could not be had upon the testimony of an accomplice unless the testimony was corroborated by such other evidence as tended to connect the defendant with the commission of the offense; (2) Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2609(E) (1981) provided that the pendency of an appeal from a conviction did not render evidence of that conviction inadmissible, and (3) when defendant objected to the introduction of evidence which was admitted, and then introduced the same evidence himself, it was no ground for reversal, even if the evidence was incompetent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence and overruled the motions for new trial.

Dutton v. State

OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to shooting and killing a bar employee during the course of a robbery. He was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed on numerous grounds. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Stafford v. State


No. F-80-256


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 131; 669 P.2d 285; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 308



September 7, 1983

DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of McClain County (Oklahoma), of three counts of murder in the first degree and was sentenced to death for each count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a change of venue should have been granted; however, trial counsel for defendant failed to follow the proper procedure to apply for a change of venue. Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 101; 668 P.2d 1126; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 279



July 11, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 19, 1983, Rehearing Denied September 19, 1983..


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Muskogee County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Hardy Summers, District Judge. DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence by the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma) for murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for an execution style murder committed in relation to a robbery in a home. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court properly declined to suppress evidence found in an impoundment search of defendant's truck when he was arrested for traffic violations as well as defendant's pre-Miranda responses to investigatory questions. Stafford v. State


No. F-79-722


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 86; 665 P.2d 1205; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 264



June 20, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 26, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Charles L. Owens, District Judge. Roger Dale Stafford, appellant, was convicted on six counts of Murder in the First Degree in Oklahoma County Case No. CRF-79-926. The jury imposed the death penalty on all counts. The appellant perfected an appeal to this Court.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) for six counts of murder in the first degree. The trial court sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, his wife, and his brother robbed a restaurant, held the employees at gunpoint, shot one employee and opened fire on the remaining employees. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction. Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.11 (1981) did not unconstitutionally shift the burden of proof to defendant when it merely required him to come forward with evidence of any mitigating circumstance. The statute did not violate the Eighth or the Fourteenth Amendment. Defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel when the alleged instances of attorney ineffectiveness concerned trial tactics and did not prejudice defendant or adversely affect the possible existence or breach any contract with his trial counsel. An ethical violation, standing alone, did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel. It was not a violation of husband-wife privilege for defendant's wife to testify when she testified only to her personal observations and conversations with her husband that were made in the presence of third persons. The evidence supported the jury's finding of four statutory aggravating circumstances and the death sentence was not excessive or disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Davis v. State


No. F-78-140, F-78-141


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 57; 665 P.2d 1186; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 237



May 9, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Davis v. Okla., 1983 U.S. LEXIS 5357 (U.S., Oct. 3, 1983)
Post-conviction relief denied at, On remand at Davis v. State, 1995 OK CR 5, 888 P.2d 1018, 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2 (Okla. Crim. App., 1995)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable David M. Cook, District Judge. Charles William Davis, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the First Degree, in Oklahoma County District Court, Cases No. CRF-77-2905 and CRF-77-2906. He was sentenced to death and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, which convicted defendant of murder in the first degree and sentenced him to death. Defendant alleged multiple errors on appeal including whether jurors were impermissibly excluded based on their beliefs regarding the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: One of the main claims on which defendant challenged his death sentence was that certain veniremen were improperly excluded from the jury because of their beliefs regarding the death penalty. The court held that the proper standard was not what the jurors' may feel about the death penalty, but that they not be irrevocably committed against imposition of the death penalty regardless of the evidence presented. The court examined the voir dire of each disputed venireman and concluded that the trial court correctly excluded them because their answers clearly indicated their inability to consider the death sentence under any circumstances. Neither was it an error for the trial court to excuse a juror when it was revealed in mid-trial that she knew two of the witnesses; the trial court's holding that an alternate juror had already been selected and that defendant would not be prejudiced by the substitution of the alternate was done after a careful examination of the facts and was within the trial court's discretion. The court held that all of defendant's 24 assignments of error were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court denied all of defendant's assignments of error and affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of first degree murder and sentence him to death.

 

975 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


McGowan v. State


No. F-81-490


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 56; 662 P.2d 1389; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 240



May 9, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Jay D. Dalton, District Judge. Douglas LeRoy McGowan, appellant, was convicted of Possession of Marijuana with Intent to Distribute in Tulsa County District Court Case No. CRF-80-0819. He was sentenced to eight years' imprisonment and a twenty-five hundred dollar ($2,500) fine and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, a violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-401(B)(2) (1975), and sentenced him to eight years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Officers armed with a search warrant for drugs entered defendant's residence and found him pointing a gun at them. After apprehending defendant, they served him with the trial court's warrant and uncovered nine plastic bags containing marijuana. Upon being convicted of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, a violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-401(B)(2) (1975), defendant appealed, arguing that the warrant was unconstitutional in that it was not served during daylight hours. The court disagreed, noting that the warrant complied with Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1230 (1981), which permitted searches at any time of the day or night. Moreover, the warrant was not a general warrant by virtue of language extending to other persons or places, as the warrant limited the search to specific items at a certain address. Moreover, statements of the prosecutor concerning the warrant did not constitute evidence of other crimes and evidentiary harpoons, as defendant did not object to testimony at trial describing the pointing of a gun and as the statement did not meet the requirements of being an evidentiary harpoon, in that it was not voluntary and not calculated to cause prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute.

Ake v. State


No. F-80-523


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 48; 663 P.2d 1; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 225



April 12, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Canadian County, Oklahoma. The Honorable James D. Bednar, District Judge. Glen Burton Ake, a/k/a Johnny Vandenover, appellant, was convicted of two counts of Murder in the First Degree and two counts of Shooting with Intent to Kill in the District Court of Canadian County, Oklahoma, Case Nos. CRF-79-302, CRF-79-303, CRF-79-304, CRF-79-305. He was sentenced to death for each murder count and to 500 years' imprisonment for each shooting with intent to kill count, and appeals.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the District Court of Canadian County, Oklahoma, which found him guilty of two counts of murder in the first degree and two counts of shooting with intent to kill.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and shooting with intent to kill. He was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that defendant failed to comply with the statutory procedure for change of venue found in Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 561 (1981) because his motion was not verified or supported by affidavit. Thus, the claim had no merit. The court also found that defendant was not entitled to a second preliminary hearing because the issue of his mental capacity and ability to assist counsel was not raised. Moreover, the original preliminary hearing did benefit defendant. The court further found that defendant should not have been treated as an insane person because of the necessity to use a drug treatment to "normalize" him. The court also found that defendant was not unfairly prejudiced by the admission of a photograph that showed how one of his victims was bound before being murdered. Defendant failed to establish any reasonable doubt as to his sanity at the time of the crime. The court also found that the death sentence was not excessive or disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

977 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Hatch v. State


No. F-80-302


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 47; 662 P.2d 1377; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 224



April 12, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Canadian County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Floyd L. Martin, District Judge. Steven Keith Hatch, a/k/a Steve Lisenbee, appellant, was convicted in Canadian County District Court of two counts of Murder in the First Degree, and two counts of Shooting with Intent to Kill. He was sentenced to forty-five (45) years' imprisonment for each count of shooting with intent to kill; and sentenced to death for each of the murder counts.



DISPOSITION: The judgments on all four charges are AFFIRMED. The sentences for Shooting with Intent to Kill are AFFIRMED. The sentences of death are VACATED and the cause REMANDED to the Canadian County District Court for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial in the District Court of Canadian County (Oklahoma), defendant was convicted of: (1) two counts of shooting with intent to kill, and given 45 years imprisonment on each count; and (2) two counts of murder in the first degree, for which he was sentenced to death. Defendant challenged the resulting judgment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised numerous challenges to his convictions and the death sentences given him. Affirming the judgment as to the convictions, the court ruled that because he did not challenge the trial court's refusal to change venue in his motion for a new trial, he failed to preserve the claim for review. Defendant's argument that the trial judge was biased and thus, should have disqualified himself from the case, was rejected because defendant failed to utilized the statutory procedure for recusal set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 20, § 1403 (1981), to which strict compliance was necessary. The claim that defense counsel was ineffective for failing to follow the proper procedure to disqualify the trial judge was also rejected because defendant had not shown that the trial judge was biased. Based on the painstaking exam of defendant with respect to his waiver of a jury trial, his claim that the waiver was not knowingly and intelligently made was deemed frivolous. However, because the trial court failed to apply an individualized consideration of defendant's character and record in imposing the death sentences, they had to be vacated and the case remanded for re-sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the death sentences imposed on defendant's two murder convictions and remanded the case for resentencing thereon. In all other respects, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

978 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Nunley v. State


No. F-80-508


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 36; 660 P.2d 1052; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 214



March 21, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Jack R. Parr, District Judge. Paul Handy Nunley, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the Second Degree, in Oklahoma County District Court, Case No. CRF-79-2282, and was sentenced to life imprisonment, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of murder in the second degree, upon a jury verdict, and sentenced him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: The victim was killed in his home, and his wife eventually confessed that she had arranged for his murder by hiring defendant to kill her husband. The trial court found defendant guilty of the murder, and he appealed, raising several arguments. The court affirmed the conviction and held, inter alia, that: (1) the warrantless search of defendant's residence was proper because there was testimony that defendant's roommate gave the officer permission to search the house; (2) the officer's testimony as to this consent was not hearsay because it was not offered to prove the truth of the matter; (3) the seizure of the address book was not unlawful because the intrusion was lawful, and the book was found by inadvertent discovery; and (4) defendant's warrantless arrest was proper because the officer had both defendant's name, and a description of defendant from the wife, who had already confessed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of second degree murder.

 

979 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Orgill v. State


No. F-80-791


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 33; 660 P.2d 649; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 211



March 16, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Joe Cannon, District Judge. Hugh Wilbert Orgill, appellant, was convicted of Distribution of a Controlled Dangerous Substance, Cocaine, in Oklahoma County District Court, Case No. CRF-80-284, was sentenced to fifteen (15) years' imprisonment, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of distribution of a controlled dangerous substance, cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, based on the testimony of two undercover police officers, was found to be the middleman in a cocaine distribution scheme. Defendant was convicted of distribution of a controlled dangerous substance, cocaine, and sentenced to 15 years of imprisonment. Defendant appealed, contending error in the admission of hearsay evidence. The court found that although a proper objection was made, no admonition was requested by defense counsel. The trial court judge also held that these hearsay statements had not been offered to prove the truth of the matter asserted. The court agreed. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred by refusing to give a requested instruction, which required the jury to find that defendant possessed a drug before he could be found guilty of its distribution. The court found no error since the requested instruction would have conflicted with a trial court instruction on aiding and abetting. The court, however, committed error in refusing to order a presentence investigation report for defendant as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 982 (1981). The court remanded for resentencing but affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment against defendant was affirmed. The case was remanded to the district court for resentencing.

 

980 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. F-78-604


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 31; 660 P.2d 634; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 209



March 3, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Garifield County, Oklahoma. The Honorable J. Russell Swanson, Judge. William Denton Jones, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the First Degree in Garfield County Case No. CRF-78-487, was sentenced to death and appeals.



DISPOSITION: The judgment and sentence is MODIFIED from death to a term of life imprisonment, and AS SO MODIFIED, is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Garfield County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of murder in the first degree and sentenced him to death. He raised numerous arguments on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder on circumstantial evidence, including his statement to a jailmate that he did not mean to kill the victim. The court rejected his arguments that certain evidence was inconsistent or lacked credibility. The preliminary hearing evidence was not required to establish a prima facie case under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, §§ 262, 264 (1981). Defendant's equal protection rights were not violated because he was not charged by grand jury indictment. He had sufficient actual notice of the aggravating circumstances supporting the death penalty to allow him to prepare a defense. The State did not impermissibly strike jurors who could not impose the death penalty. The court did not err in admitting the jailmate's statement because defendant was not provided a copy. The State's medical expert was not insufficiently qualified. While a medical record was admitted in error without a proper custodian's testimony, its admission was not prejudicial. The court upheld the constitutionality of the death penalty statutes. Upon review of the appropriateness of the death penalty pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13 (1981), the court reduced the sentence to life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder in the first degree but modified the sentence from death to a term of life imprisonment. As so modified, the judgment was affirmed.

 

981 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Pegg v. State


No. M-81-33


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 26; 659 P.2d 370; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 205



February 23, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Comanche County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Peter Clinton Moore, Special District Judge. Larry Pegg, appellant, was convicted of Communicating False Rumors in Comanche County District Court, Case No. CRM-80-592. He was sentenced to one hundred and twenty (120) days in jail and a fine of five hundred ($500.00) dollars, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of communicating false rumors pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 781 (1981) and sentenced defendant to 120 days in jail and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's automobile was observed with a sticker attached to the rear bumper that contained the name of the personnel manager of defendant's employer, followed by the word "prostitute." The trial court convicted defendant of communicating false rumors pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 781 (1981) and sentenced defendant to 120 days in jail and a fine. Defendant appealed, contending that he was convicted under a statute that was void for vagueness and overbroad and that the trial court record did not reflect that defendant's self-representation was preceded by a knowing and voluntary waiver of the right to counsel. On appeal, the court held that the ordinary person and defendant were apprised by § 781 of the type of conduct that was proscribed -- the intentional disparagement of the reputation or character of another by a false communication, that the conduct proscribed by § 781 implied a knowledge of the falsity of the rumor or report and was limited to the communication of facts, and that defendant was adequately informed by the trial court of his right to counsel and made a knowing and voluntary waiver of his right to counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had convicted defendant of communicating false rumors.

 

982 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Childers v. City of Tulsa


No. M-82-87


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1983 OK CR 15; 658 P.2d 497; 1983 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 192



February 7, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the Tulsa Municipal Criminal Court. The Honorable John S. Turner, Municipal Court Judge. Johnny Lee Childers, appellant, was convicted in Tulsa Municipal Criminal Court of Refusing to Leave Public Property Forthwith After Demand by a Peace Officer, Case No. 326601. He was sentenced to serve five (5) days in the City Jail with credit for time served and a one-hundred dollar ($100) fine.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction, by the Tulsa Municipal Criminal Court (Oklahoma), for refusing to leave public property forthwith after demand by a police officer, in violation of Tulsa, Okla., Rev. Ordinances tit. 27, § 511B(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed in the main downtown mall asking for money from passersby. A City police officer approached him and requested that he leave the mall area, and arrested him when he refused to obey the officer's demand. On appeal, defendant contended that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court reversed the judgment and ordered that the case be dismissed. It reasoned that because the ordinance was devoid of any guidelines as to when an officer could demand that a person to leave a city park or other public property, it gave unbridled discretion to law enforcement officials to determine what conduct would be disallowed on public property and encouraged arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. The court further reasoned that a plain reading of the ordinance revealed that the enacting legislative body intended § 511B(3) to constitute an independent public offense, separate from the earlier subsections prohibiting public drunkenness, so that a person could be punished for merely failing to leave public property once a peace officer demanded that he leave. The court concluded that the ordinance was repugnant to both the federal and state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with instructions to dismiss.

 

983 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Ring v. State


No. F-81-711


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 200; 654 P.2d 1085; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 384



December 10, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Homer Smith, District Judge. George Leon Ring, appellant, was convicted of Robbery with Firearms and Assault and Battery with a Dangerous Weapon, in Oklahoma County District Court, Case No. CRF-80-5041, was sentenced to twenty-five (25) and five (5) years' imprisonment, respectively, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted and sentenced him for robbery with firearms and assault and battery with a dangerous weapon.


OVERVIEW: A taxicab driver testified that defendant pulled a gun on him and ordered him to take him to a certain destination. Upon arrival, defendant robbed the driver and took the cab. Defendant fired a shot and drove off as a police car approached. The officer pursued the fleeing taxi, and an officer was shot when shots were later fired by defendant. On appeal from his conviction, defendant claimed that he was denied his constitutional right of due process of law, as guaranteed by the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments, because the trial court failed to certify him as a child, and that Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104.2 (1981) created a presumption that he was an "adult" in the eyes of the law and shifted the burden to him to prove that he was a child. The court rejected this argument, finding that the statute was constitutional, and that it did not create such a presumption. The court also held that the classification created by the legislature had a rational relationship to an important governmental objective, i.e., protecting the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

984 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Brooks v. State


No. F-80-280


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 179; 654 P.2d 1054; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 399



November 15, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Kingfisher County, Oklahoma. The Honorable J. Russell Swanson, District Judge. Troy Brooks, appellant, was convicted of Assault and Battery with a Deadly Weapon, in Kingfisher County District Court, Case No. CFR-77-56, was sentenced to two (2) years' imprisonment, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Kingfisher County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of assault and battery with a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the criminal division of the district court was without jurisdiction to try him because he was 17 years old when he allegedly committed the assault. The court disagreed. An information was filed on November 9, 1977. Thereafter, it was discovered that defendant was under 18 years of age, and on January 18, 1978, a certification hearing was ordered, which resulted in his certification to stand trial as an adult. The actions of the district court were in accordance with Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1112 (1981). Defendant also alleged that he was denied his right to a speedy hearing. He relied upon a prior case in which the court found a 20 month delay to be a denial of the right to a speedy hearing. The court disagreed and found that the delay was six months as compared to 20 months in the other case. Furthermore, the reasons for the delay were that defendant spent 2 months in the hospital; he changed counsel; it was not readily ascertained that he was a juvenile; and one time his attorney was not present at the time the certification hearing had been scheduled. Moreover, defendant failed to demonstrate that he was prejudiced by the delay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for assault and battery with a deadly weapon.

 

985 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Colbert v. State


No. F-80-419


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 174; 654 P.2d 624; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 359



November 5, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Carter County. The Honorable Thomas S. Walker, Associate District Judge. Charles Colbert, Jr., appellant, was convicted of Manslaughter in the First Degree in Carter County District Court Case No. CRF-78-269. He was sentenced to eight (8) years' imprisonment and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Carter County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of manslaughter in the first degree in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 711 (1981). Defendant argued that Okla. Stat. tit. 22, §§ 1171-1174 (1971), which governed the determination of defendant's competence to stand trial, violated his substantive and procedural due process rights under the United States and Oklahoma Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: While reading defendant his Miranda rights, the arresting officers asked defendant if he understood why he was under arrest, and defendant admitted to killing the victim. Defendant was committed to a state mental hospital pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, §§ 1171-1174 (1971), by application of defense counsel, for observation and a determination of his competency to stand trial. A state psychiatrist found that defendant was of extremely low intelligence, but that he was mentally competent. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that a full evidentiary hearing under §§ 1171-1174 as to defendant's competence was not required to meet the requirements of due process. Defendant was competent to waive a jury trial, and the trial judge had authority to conduct the trial without a jury. Defendant's privilege against self-incrimination was not violated because his admission that he killed the victim did not occur in a custodial interrogation. Evidence seized pursuant to defendant's confession, and pursuant to a search conducted with the consent of defendant's father, was properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant.

 

986 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


No. F-80-581


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 165; 653 P.2d 937; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 401



October 13, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected on Denial of Rehearing December 2, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Jack R. Parr, District Judge. Guy Granville Williams, appellant, was convicted in Oklahoma County District Court of Grand Larceny After Former Conviction of Three Felonies, Case No. CRF-79-2752. He was sentenced to twenty (20) years' imprisonment, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for grand larceny after former conviction of three felonies from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) and subsequent sentence to 20 years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his girlfriend entered a jewelry store, ostensibly to purchase a diamond engagement ring. The salesperson stated that when she asked if she could help them, defendant replied that, "he wanted to see a round diamond in a carat-and-a-half size (1.5)." The salesperson showed them two diamonds. After defendant and his girlfriend had left the store, the diamonds were weighed. What was supposed to be a 1.48 carat diamond was instead a synthetic cubic zirconium, weighing 2.67 carats. There was further testimony that a 2.60 carat cubic zirconium was equivalent in size to a 1.5 carat diamond, and whoever switched the diamond with the cubic zirconium was most probably aware of this fact. On appeal from a conviction for grand larceny after former conviction of three felonies, the court affirmed. The factual circumstances when considered together were inconsistent with the innocence of the accused and were sufficient to support a conviction on circumstantial evidence. Also, the mere fact that a codefendant attempted to escape punishment by inculpating the defendant was not a sufficient ground for severance. A motion for severance was within the discretion of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for grand larceny after former conviction of three felonies and sentence to 20 years of imprisonment.

Parks v. State


No. F-79-3


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 132; 651 P.2d 686; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 339



August 26, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 28, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Joe Cannon, District Judge. Robyn LeRoy Parks, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the First Degree in Oklahoma County District Court, Case No. CRF-77-3159. He was sentenced to death and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of murder in the first degree and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: During taped phone conversations with an informant, defendant stated that he had killed a gas station employee who had written down his license plate because he was afraid that the employee would call the police when he realized that his credit card was fraudulent. Defendant was found guilty of first degree murder and, after a hearing on aggravating and mitigating circumstances, the jury voted to impose the death penalty. The court affirmed and held that the State properly established the corpus delecti by evidence independent of defendant's statements. The court found that the trial court correctly refused to give an instruction on second degree murder because the evidence was insufficient to support a lesser included offense. The court ruled that there was no error in admitting the taped conversations because the informant had consented to the taping and the best evidence rule was not violated. The court concluded that the state death penalty statute was constitutional, that the sentence was not imposed under any arbitrary factor, that the evidence supported the finding of an aggravating circumstance, and that the sentence was not excessive or disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's judgment of conviction and the sentence imposed thereon.

Brewer v. State


No. F-79-609


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 128; 650 P.2d 54; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 325



August 18, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 20, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Raymond W. Graham, Judge. Benjamin Brewer, appellant, was charged and convicted of Murder in the First Degree, was sentenced to death, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction on charges by the State for murder in the first degree pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981) and his sentence to death by the jury in the District Court of Tulsa County, (Oklahoma) on grounds that he was denied a fair trial based on conduct by the prosecutor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on first-degree murder charges for the stabbing death of a woman. Defendant challenged conduct by the prosecutor during trial and sentencing. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction by the trial court and granted defendant a new trial. The court reversed defendant's conviction for outrageous behavior by the prosecutor during trial that was prejudicial to defendant and deprived him of a fair trial. The prosecutor's display of stabbing the victim's photograph with the murder weapon during cross-examination of a defense witness was outrageous and did not fall within the wide range of free speech and illustration allowed to a prosecutor. The trial court's comments to the jury did not cure the prejudice to defendant caused by the prosecutor's ridicule to objections by defendant's attorney. During the sentencing hearing, the prosecutor twice referred to the possibility that defendant would commit similar crimes in the future if acquitted without meeting the obligation of the State under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.12(7) (1981) to list such a propensity in the bill of particulars. The court addressed evidentiary issues pertinent to the retrial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction by the trial court and remanded the case for a new trial.

Pitts v. State


Nos. F-81-370, F-81-371


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 121; 649 P.2d 788; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 319



August 6, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 8, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Jay Dalton, District Judge. Opie Donnell Pitts, II, and TIMOTHY ALVESTER GAFFNEY, appellants, were convicted conjointly of the crime of Robbery With a Dangerous Weapon, in the District Court of Tulsa County, Case Number CRF-80-2042, and sentenced to five (5) years' imprisonment, the Honorable Jay Dalton, presiding. Both appellants were sentenced to five (5) years' imprisonment, and appeal.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which convicted them conjointly of the crime of robbery with a dangerous weapon and sentenced them to five years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was informed by a robbery victim, moments after she had been robbed, that the perpetrator had fled down a particular street in a gray Grand Prix. The officer had seen the identified car pulling out of the same area just prior to the report and began pursuit, pulling over the subject car. After the first defendant was frisked, the officer observed the second defendant crouching in the car. A search was conducted and defendants were arrested. On defendants' appeals from their convictions for robbery with a dangerous weapon, the court affirmed. The court first held that defendants' argument that Okla. R. Ct. Crim. App. 6 was unconstitutional was meritless because Rule 6 had previously been upheld and was not in conflict with Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1053 (1981). The officer had probable cause to make the warrantless arrest under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 196 (1981) considering the timing of the patrol, the robbery, the report, the fact that the car was proceeding in the direction the victim had pointed, and that it was in fact a gray Grand Prix. A can of mace pointed at the victim during the robbery constituted a dangerous weapon under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 801 (1981).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences.

 

990 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Spitznas v. State


No. H-82-225


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 115; 648 P.2d 1271; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 313



July 29, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An original proceeding in habeas corpus. Petitioner was denied bail pending appeal in Garfield County District Court in Case No. CRF-81-2, and requested issuance of the Writ of Habeas Corpus for bail pending appeal.



DISPOSITION:  Writs Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner, who was denied bail pending appeal in the Garfield County District Court (Oklahoma), brought an original proceeding requesting issuance of a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner had been convicted of rape and sodomy and sentenced to 15 years imprisonment. Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1077 (1981) provided that bail on appeal was not allowed after conviction for rape. The prisoner claimed that the statute as applied to him was unconstitutional. The court rejected the claim and denied the prisoner the relief sought. There was no fundamental right to bail pending appeal, and so the rational basis test applied to determine whether the legislature's classification was related to a legitimate state interest. Because § 1077 provided a rational means to insure that those persons convicted of the most serious of offenses would not flee by denying appeal bond, and the classification of offenses deemed serious enough to be included was not wholly irrelevant to that objective, there was no equal protection violation. The court also concluded that the statute was not void for vagueness, did not violate the separation of powers doctrine in Okla. Const. art. IV, § 1 because there existed only a statutory right and no constitutional right to bail on appeal, and, as applied to the prisoner was not an unconstitutional ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ.

 

991 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. State


No. F-80-632


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 114; 648 P.2d 1268; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 312



July 27, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Pottawatomie County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Donald E. Powers, District Judge. Carl Dean Hill, appellant, was convicted of Burglary in the Second Degree, After Former Conviction of Two or More Felonies, in the District Court of Pottawatomie County, Case No. CRF-79-341. He was sentenced to thirty-five (35) years' imprisonment and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Pottawatomie County, Oklahoma, which convicted him of burglary in the second degree, after former conviction of two or more felonies and sentenced him to 35 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with burglary, and he did not testify in his own behalf. After he was convicted, the State alleged 19 prior convictions of defendant for enhancement purposes. The court affirmed his conviction and sentence. Defendant's Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination was not violated by the trial judge's failure to give a special cautionary instruction to the jury regarding his decision not to testify in his own behalf. The defense failed to make a request for such an instruction. Admission of certain portions of defendant's penitentiary records to prove a former conviction under Oklahoma's Habitual Criminal Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 51 (1981), was not prejudicial. Nothing was admitted into evidence from the prison records except fingerprint cards and prison photographs, which was an acceptable method of proving identification. Because there was no proof that defendant had been represented by counsel for six prior convictions, the court struck such convictions. However, because 13 prior convictions were properly admitted, the effect of the admission of the six prior convictions was merely cumulative and did not require modification of his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Browning v. State


No. F-80-521


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 113; 648 P.2d 1261; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 311



July 26, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Comanche County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Jack Brock, Judge. WILL BENNETT BROWNING, appellant, was convicted of Burglary in the Second Degree in Comanche County District Court, Case No. CRF-78-1366. He was sentenced to thirty years' imprisonment and appeals.



DISPOSITION: Sentence modified to twenty-five years' imprisonment and as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the District Court of Comanche County, (Oklahoma) for burglary in the second degree. He was sentenced to 30 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary in the second degree, after former conviction of two felonies, and he was sentenced to 30 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed. Defendant's sentence was modified from 30 years imprisonment to 25 years imprisonment and, as modified, affirmed. The court held that there was no error in allowing the refiling of an information after the initial information was dismissed for lack of prosecution. Further, the police officer's testimony that he "saw him at the other trial that he had and preliminary" was not an evidentiary harpoon. The court noted that even when the information of a prior crime did not allude to previous convictions, it should not be used as proof of a former conviction by the fact that it served no purpose but to advise the jury of details of previous crimes. The reference to other charges that did not result in a conviction required a reduction in defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was modified from 30 years imprisonment to 25 years imprisonment and, as modified, affirmed.

 

993 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Gilbert v. State


No. M-80-314


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 100; 648 P.2d 1226; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 300



July 1, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Joe Cannon, Judge. Fred P. Gilbert, appellant, was convicted of Direct Contempt of Court of Oklahoma County District Court Case No. CJ-80-259. He was sentenced to six (6) months in the county jail and a Three Thousand Dollar ($3,000) fine, and appeals.



DISPOSITION: The judgment and sentence is REVERSED AND REMANDED with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted the attorney of contempt of court.


OVERVIEW: The attorney presented the trial judge with a motion to disqualify. The motion contained many outrageous and disrespectful allegations against the judge. The judge found the attorney to be in contempt of court and sentenced the attorney to six months in jail and a $ 3,000 fine. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the contempt conviction was improper because the acts constituting the contempt did occur in the "immediate view and presence" of the trial court, as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 585 (1981). The attorney's actual drafting of the motion to disqualify did not occur in the presence of the trial court, and thus, the contempt conviction was improper. Only the delivery of the motion to disqualify occurred "in the presence of the court." The court held that the drafting, filing, and presenting of the offensive motion were all required before the alleged contempt was completed. Because the record reflected that the delivery of the motion did not in itself cause any disorder in the trial court's proceedings, or that the attorney displayed any insolent behavior at the hearing, the misconduct did not constitute direct contempt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted the attorney of contempt of court.

 

994 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


No. F-80-582


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 95; 647 P.2d 450; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 293



June 18, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Tillman County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Weldon Ferris, District Judge. The appellant, John Leon Davis, was convicted in the District Court of Tillman County in CRF-79-91 for the offense of Making Lewd and Indecent Proposals to a Child Under the Age of Fourteen, After Former Conviction of a Felony, was sentenced to twenty (20) years' imprisonment, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the District Court of Tillman County (Oklahoma) on charges that he committed the offense of making lewd and indecent proposals to a child under the age of 14 in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1123 (1971), after a former conviction of a felony, and sentenced him to serve 20 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant came to his door naked and pulled a six year-old girl inside and requested that she grab his penis. The girl immediately ran to a neighbor and related what had just happened. Defendant was charged with an indecency crime. At trial, he objected to the admission of the neighbor to whom the girl recounted what had happened. The trial court allowed the testimony and convicted defendant. Affirming, the court held that the victim was properly qualified to testify at trial because she was a competent witness pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2601 (1981). The court ruled that the testimony of the neighbor was admissible because it was not hearsay pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2801(4)(b)(1) (1981), but that even if it were it would have qualified as an excited utterance exception pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2803(2) (1981). The court found that defendant, by entering a plea of not guilty, waived all defects in the information except those going to jurisdiction. The court concluded that defendant, who was 55 years old, was properly charged under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1123 (1971) and failed to establish a denial of his equal protection because of sex discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

995 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State v. Koo


No. O-81-75


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 93; 647 P.2d 889; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 289



June 16, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 12, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Thomas Walker, Associate District Judge. Gary Koo and Anthony Salvatore Jacene, appellees, were charged in Cleveland County District Court individually on several counts of Commercial Gambling, State v. Jacene, CRF-80-300, CRF-80-319; State v. Koo, CRF-80-322, CRF-80-325, CRF-80-326, CRF-80-333, but a demurrer to the charges was sustained by the magistrate and district judge, and the State appeals.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision by the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which affirmed a magistrate's judgment that sustained a demurrer by defendants on several counts of commercial gambling with which defendants were charged.


OVERVIEW: In each information defendants were charged with the crime of commercial gambling and the appeals by the State were consolidated. The magistrate found that in each case, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 982A-1, A-2 (1981), were unconstitutionally vague and indefinite. The magistrate further found that Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 981.4 (1981), which defined a "gambling place" to be unconstitutionally broad and vague. The magistrate also found the information to be so duplicitous as to be unclear and uncertain as to the offense allegedly committed. It was the district court judge's decision that Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 982 was so broad in its scope and vague in its application that it was unconstitutional. The court agreed that the district court was correct in finding that the offense described in each information stated an offense pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 982A-2 (Supp. 1980), as opposed to § 982 A-1. The contention that to be constitutional the statute had to specifically state a requirement of knowledge, intent, or guilty purpose was without merit. Also, the terms "receive," "bet," and "chance" were clearly understood by all and were not lacking in either specificity or clarity.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

996 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Webb v. State


No. F-80-713


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 90; 647 P.2d 440; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 292



June 15, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Seminole County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Donald E. Powers, Judge. Michael Edward Webb, appellant, was convicted in Seminole County District Court, Case No. CRF-79-252, for the offense of Burglary in the Second Degree, sentenced to seven (7) years' imprisonment and appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Seminole County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of burglary in the second degree. Defendant was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had abandoned an automobile in the citizen's driveway. Items from a burglary were found when the vehicle was impounded and an inventory search conducted. Defendant denied ownership of the automobile even though he was the person to whom the automobile was released after impoundment. Defendant was convicted of burglary in the second degree and was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment. Defendant appealed. The court noted the statutory presumption that a person in possession of stolen property knew it to be stolen, and thus found no error with jury instructions based on that statutory presumption. The court also noted that circumstantial evidence was admissible as long as every reasonable hypothesis other than that of guilt was excluded by the circumstantial evidence. The court also noted that defendant had not presented evidence to refute his guilt at trial. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment and sentence against defendant.

 

997 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Wofford v. State


No. F-80-461


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 83; 646 P.2d 1300; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 282



June 11, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Stephens County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Ellen Colclasure Steely, Associate Judge. Ernest Buzzy Wofford, appellant, was convicted of Burglary in the Second Degree in Stephens County District Court Case No. CRF-79-16. He was sentenced to two (2) years imprisonment, and appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Stephens County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of burglary in the second degree under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1435 (1981). He was sentenced to two years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of burglary in the second degree pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1435 (1981). On appeal, he alleged that Okla. Unif. Jury Instructions Crim. No. 5 was fundamentally erroneous because it gave rise to a mandatory presumption of his intent to steal. The court held that defendant failed to object to the instruction or request an alternative instruction during trial. The court concluded the instruction was not so fundamentally defective as to deprive defendant of a fair and impartial trial. The question of his intent during the commission of the crime was established by overwhelming evidence. The court ruled that defendant did not request an instruction on voluntary intoxication, as the defense was not supported by the evidence; therefore, in light of the evidence of guilt, the instruction did not rise to the level of fundamental error. The court concluded that because defendant had three prior felony convictions, he was ineligible under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 991(a)(B) (1980) for a suspended sentence. Thus, defendant was not prejudiced by the trial court's failure to instruct the jury on his inability to receive a suspended sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for burglary in the second degree.

 

998 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. F-80-100


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 37; 665 P.2d 815; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 405



March 12, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion on Rehearing February 8, 1983, Reported at: 665 P.2d 815 at 826.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Jay D. Dalton, Judge. Kenneth Ray Johnson, appellant, was convicted of Murder in the First Degree. He was sentenced to death, and appeals.



DISPOSITION: The jury's verdict of guilty is AFFIRMED. The death sentence is vacated. This cause shall be REMANDED to the district court for a new sentencing proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction and sentence by the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma), for murder in the first degree. Defendant was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed a store clerk during a robbery. He was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and vacated the sentence. The court held that there was probable cause for defendant's warrantless arrest based on statements of defendant's friend. It was proper to exclude a juror who was irrevocably committed against the imposition of the death penalty. Statements made by the victim just prior to his death were admissible under the hearsay exception for excited utterances. Relevant evidence of other crimes by defendant was relevant at the punishment stage to enable the jury to determine whether to impose life imprisonment or the death penalty. However, the court vacated the sentence because certain evidence tending to show that another killing by defendant was in self-defense was improperly excluded. It should have been admitted in mitigation of the death penalty. The trial court also erred by admitting evidence of two other killings because the State failed to notify defendant prior to trial that it was going to use the evidence. Also, the aggravating circumstance that the murder was committed for remuneration was improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated the death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding.

 

999 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re Champeau


Nos. H-82-103, H-82-105, H-82-109


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 33; 643 P.2d 326; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 223



March 5, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An original proceeding in habeas corpus. Petitioners were denied bail pending appeal in Pottawatomie County District Court in Case Nos. CRF-80-290, CRF-80-288, and CRF-80-289, and request issuance of the Writ of Habeas Corpus for bail pending appeal.



DISPOSITION: WRITS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought bail pending appeal from their convictions for unlawful cultivation of marijuana and unlawful possession of marijuana with intent to distribute. Defendants requested issuance of a writ of habeas corpus for bail pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendants had in their possession four tons of marijuana. The offenses for which defendants were convicted were not listed among those contained in Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1077 (Supp. 1981), for which bail pending appeal was required to be denied. On review, the court rejected defendants' argument that the statute was unconstitutional for vagueness and denied the petitions. The court interpreted the statute as being a statement of legislative policy which left to the trial judge the exercise of his discretion whether or not bail pending appeal should be allowed. The trial judge, after having heard all the testimony and after considering all the evidence, and recognizing that the consequences of the offenses were of sufficient gravity to the general public, determined that bail pending appeal should be denied. The court held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion when he denied bail. The court determined that the legislative intent expressed by § 1077 left the matter of bail pending appeal within the discretion of the trial judge, except that the trial judge was required to state the reason why bail was granted in each case.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writs.

 

1000 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Pratt v. State


No. M-79-699


Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma


1982 OK CR 31; 642 P.2d 268; 1982 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 236



March 4, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Pittsburg County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Clyde E. Davis, Judge. J. C. Pratt, appellant, was convicted of Keeping a Disorderly House in Pittsburg County District Court, Case No. M-79-699. He was sentenced to six (6) months' imprisonment and a five hundred dollar ($ 500.00) fine and appeals.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Pittsburg County (Oklahoma) that convicted him of keeping a disorderly house in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1026 (1971) and sentenced him to six months' imprisonment and a $ 500 fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's neighbors testified that they were subjected to or confronted with loud and raucous music, public drunkenness, urination in public, fist fights, shouting of obscenities, and automobile racing. Defendant was convicted of keeping a disorderly house in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1026 (1971). Defendant contended that the terms "peace, comfort or decency" were subject to multiple definitions and rendered § 1026 unconstitutionally vague and totally incomprehensible to a person of ordinary intelligence. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court ruled that § 1026 was not so vague as to be violative of due process. The court could not say that the activities emanating from or associated with the occupants or guests of defendant's residence did not in fact breach or disturb the peace or tranquility of the neighborhood as contemplated by § 1026 or that a person of ordinary intelligence would not have known in advance that these activities were prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence.
